Around Ads With Subscriptions

 

The Financial Times has reached a new high with subscribers at 629,000, a 5% increase year over year, according to The Guardian's Roy Greenslade. Although the company continues to struggle with ad sales like most print publishers, the company has achieved profitability. Pearson, the parent company, said in its interim report that digital subscriptions are up 24%. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqUKZKN8AZ6HHhQZAyVeubnPNm6uQRLP4XiSesqRm4yx19QWaDn_t8A-agkZsHgYc7s57FFjQcQJL71p52SSHn8Q42Xc8yzff2AxLrlxZ23W7jo3VaLpPlYKlqxQkjCg-5YIwyt7ekgLt3Fg4-ZZgcPaGbHoVSp1Cw1fZzfXsbAeIIVB2LYeH6z4thTT7DjeiNNfswUiGMckppT3r9j6Cdp3E8OWGnmPekz0=> .

 

Pin Sales

 

Pinterest is playing around with a new feature called "related pins," which could lead to its impending ad strategy, VentureBeat's Meghan Kelly reports. The new pins will also come with the option to give feedback. By giving a thumbs up or down, users can tell Pinterest whether they want to see more pins like that. Pinterest gets lumped into the social group, but it's driving a fair amount of ecommerce, which differentiates it from the other giants like Facebook and Twitter. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqUIwOQUSOXZzf4e1DIj8QICjXjzmYD6qTq0tuaEUc0gNnBJ8NAuo1MTAxtt5QYDI5uWsCbn1Ee6JxBjMMDkzSR8KytDym37Sz_f39lUd6_8rJSx7JwDPoEj2kq_K61hQ5C0DZ99j3M5z0EIr09diOUv6RPaGYMNqydQ=> .

 

A Facebook Debate

 

Rob Leathern, CEO of Optimal, takes to Business Insider to tell why he doesn't feel the Forrester Report about Facebook <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqUIt0xzTlZikZm9SzDtzj5_xw9bLuUckoTmhngbpbohtNsqCmYGdhq6xqMdunBXBN_WUZZDi_XlF_LBzk5asRYEl5sb6ZuwHRnvyvFceSXRxTjLW2pkDE3bdd745Uy7M7WKY7HK0gX76svo81D1_iI8J1r7607Rts1jUGXhpReJXMONs4-0s3gWIi-zUNXEmUdHDQ2v8BsvpDIh15xS7kQYk9M6UZEs6uxE=>  is accurate or fair. He writes, "In the unfortunate all-too-common-lately style of high-level broad spurious insights without any detailed methodology, most of the actual 'data' is only available behind a paywall, but there was enough publicly available to see some of the major issues with it and then the benefit of reading the report compelled me to speak out here." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqULsMzBUOG0MkFPxQmKONjtJtvcY0ACSKJAfOtzKTEKpsXEipLLt7sMxaLDFW9YrerZwqSsTk2Sqbfe5YHQf5vGni0WP-2yY0U42cuYc2udpczmOmqQZF39y3VOUs-cdslVMWJpGCOmwvqWY9RWgrDIg0hmfEP62msU47BwqUY3sTQyBQgRghkdT0gY_TIfcFvtw8mOfHfvunQ==> .

 

Clickthrough Klout

 

Klout and Mass Relevance are forming a partnership that will allows broadcast networks to use tweets from "highly ranked" Twitter users during television shows or in paid campaigns. "The Klout score becomes another criterion for brands and broadcasters to filter and use tweets," says Tyler Singletary, director of platform at Klout. "People who see content from Klout influencers are two times more likely to click through to an advertiser's page." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqUK2nSPK2avMNwzXY7KoXIRaRBoyT2oqehYJJwwM62jxn2_8nSa7N4smkWAnpbheKk17HRqdGwOiH0OimTlQ6zy6ZK5ls2hwF3AWyEdwAAubv2IaFmkih2zrvZY01Hpw3tEnSaFNVk2ePsSLVrh-hzPYsQqdS69O1fg_fcGnS6U-qKuqppA_cuuUsa9ZRQyYh0QmNKNg1cBGqG2H2Uaw2VvnfKsy-9sAw9kkd0nOVws3x2BWvwE-9ZTz> .

 

Consulting Consolidation

 

Professional services firm PricewaterhouseCoopers (PwC) will acquire management-consulting firm Booz & Co. pending approvals from Booz stakeholders, GigaOm reported today. Although PwC plays heavily in the accounting and tax-services space, it foreseeably gains enterprise strategy consulting and digital-technology services strength in Booz & Co. As GigaOM's Barb Darrow details, PwC does an estimated $32 billion in business annually; Booz's estimated revenue is $1 billion. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zz8ZzjKbqUJeKImV57bcjKT2T8WRLNtQjOW7CNujfKaVs5R5NuQ7IGelkPAwLmGa_fsTHaP4Vk1M_Psxz16TgWkFB0aGCwwFHD6Qs8C6CQ-qMhO_AO2bLG9GbOwaPcH68C5PJoY_iAcn-_W3xkwJJ8DBoZtGy83PZaFrXKIAsNt3iIC8NGkuBzvLddln5W2h913-l4elB8tv7Z2J8_bGUX5S6NjcvIZB> .

Sociomantic's CRM Play

 

Ecommerce retargeting firm Sociomantic is teaming up with Revenue Management Systems to serve personalized ads online through Sociomantic's CRM system. "Synchronizing customer data and inventory information with digital marketing lets travel suppliers reach the right consumers in real time, with offers just right for who they are, their travel intent and their place in the purchase funnel," said Eric Nordling, COO of Revenue Management Systems. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFIT1_LLy_4L1W_wvsGHrRM5BuB75KfDeJvD_frnk7-1vjfKsxYw6KUUusQE0pOcBQrQIGnqzX-7DL2rbFQ03PN-jOfHgD1y8BvWQ4MVIQ7iaqp8b3ccN39iMCNYNxOHs5scsdu9f7g57r2j8PGGPcla> .

 

Twitter Programmatic

 

Last Saturday, Ameet Ranadive, product manager at Twitter, went long form in a post on Medium titled "Demystifying Programmatic Marketing and RTB." Ranadive starts by defining: "At a high level, Programmatic Marketing is the practice of implementing an automated set of business rules to efficiently target your most valuable customers and prospects with personalized ads." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFK91lZV86nOP_G4Mubb2puj2v0mR-kByWJsrb42y4iaMr5hjuFo-XSIdIpq5nZQf5bA6jOgoilVMkNfTRZ4-2cw2IzLC-Gr_VsyhZW846qGXhRlTS24MmKmrPU22D1tlhU=> . Insights on Twitter's programmatic future.

 

Cookies Down

 

There is a general sentiment in the advertising world that the end of the third-party cookie is near, but the biggest tech companies could expedite the process by building their own tracking tools, The Wall Street Journal's Elizabeth Dwoskin points out. Microsoft, Google and Facebook are all in the process of developing cross-device tracking technology that would be more powerful than third-party cookies, and would likely have more robust opt-out options for consumers. "There is a Battle Royal brewing," said Scott Meyer, chief executive of Evidon Inc. "Whoever controls access to all that data can charge rent for it - and has a tremendous advantage going forward." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFL3yNGh4Uo9CQkMpJat4bUkOWkM4KdX7zIQQqPscAIO7zo8VMA7xNWPG81SvBiGlKFdXRSH_1WNDVU8w1zLpQ1aD2k6gaipoqczpebmX6YOhTpnFcx9vf9YC-_CqfdtOdX-nT40Rs9QrhSDSRUbg-dRfoWjeNjCVLZJzCFzYgzbIkwTM-e9km8wwZUH-lkKUdY=> .

 

DNT Children

 

Children, and even babies, are spending more time online due to mobile device proliferation, so Sen. Edward Markey, D-Mass., and Rep. Joe Barton, R-Texas, are introducing a "Do Not Track Kids" Act as an update to the Children's Online Privacy Protection Act. The updated provision would prevent advertisers from serving targeted ads to anyone under 15 and would also allow kids and parents to erase collected information online. Read the senator's release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFJSJ2m3xWA6ZeA3UuAjHZW317E2BTPVmWynQZXET9b3mMEIO4CahalcC7glGXFJZ19Pqfix6mlld9kDUnS-tBHLdd_us3k64J6V-Mk9cqN8acGSdJOX3y58v2ln-HGATdLZWOJ1RpworWA7kq16TYfT> .

 

Loyal Acquisition

 

First Data has acquired Perka, a cardless loyalty program, AllThingsD's Kara Swisher reports. "The loyalty industry is quickly changing with the advent of mobile everywhere, from being proprietary and closed, to open," said Perka CEO Alan Chung about the deal. "We saw a real synergy with First Data and of their vision going forward, in which loyalty is a critical component as a tool of local merchants." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFIWBpvjBohL_YxhDIm08C5WPMBYp31QdDDtv_-imKrUopctUBHMQdYfjh7CxPD5f0O-kjVPSlW-TC1c95EJ0nIPm-rld-wNVE-k_8n-iI3TpMFRC5Qrh7z7RQLTPf_X-d1dd3EzV0oRK8uZFPyB7Ss9n3yixGIOhl0629lA_IWDIqZMCjwu3HgNeP5nq8MAqgOs7w9mR83tVA==> .

LinkedIn: A Very Mobile Q3

 

LinkedIn saw its Marketing Solutions business hit $89 million - a 38% year-over-year increase. With the late-July launch of self-serve native ad units, content marketing continues to drive interest from marketers. Although it's still new, the number of customers running Sponsored Updates campaigns is now over 1,000, and two-thirds of it is mobile due to higher CTRs, executives said on the Q3 earnings call. Thirty-eight percent of unique LinkedIn visitors now come through mobile. Earnings release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFLT86kIJI48PzdFGtzWIZAxqvy3gwPjfrbNFEKBxHIRUpxddLvR-CsqHpZAf-D1DOyOdhE5okG8CXEXh-wSQqHDemXhpdwO3fhWeZw67ASX63y5p34b-vIIyZxnp1-Ic8sPA8VaW3bIMLLNidcxZ6BnalH1TQxQj1Qn5-QD-lCYvMkg4__5LsVmSgDIMxqESgLaMBv9UzBj9yPDGPwxtZTn> 

 

IAB Tryin' Hard Enough?

 

Chief Digital Investment Officer Ari Bluman of WPP's media group, GroupM, takes a critical look at the Interactive Advertising Bureau (IAB) and various industry pain points in an AdAge op-ed. "Overall, is IAB doing enough? Progress could be faster, but it's doing better than anyone else. None of what IAB and its members are doing will satisfy marketers if the recommendations aren't quickly put into practice. If sellers don't adopt the viewable impression and the Quality Assurance Guidelines as soon as possible, the whole industry will be held down." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001rbvoVX4swFKPHctdmxMPtOdUleiGT2PHq6muEr4Qo4Vz7ftReXNcszdT6knY01vcD86S6jBRnyWzCoEoIYghPYh4pWkMHRY_ZK8rZ67O_lZN4BazCQvTp4HSWbEzFAtMV1CtqtKUcU_HxZHPJb9tajdkftsYxQ6m> .

Ads, Photos And Instagram

 

Time's Alex Fitzpatrick takes a look at some new Pew Research  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAeubSXCbzq2d27yvi_nfKffZq5P3dGfB4kcwZ3HNtIUC4kCYkMIKGqPkL1Ng5bEO1taLdxPEziFwZjDTVGLOiVmBaOTqfq3MM4Q96sT4jk75nPEOuZWf2LkQlkOA3nlWKtH9l0wCP5n_Z_W09Tl-YjKbPEmaPymNu6o=> findings on photos and video online in a short feature article. He writes, "You say you're a brand looking to advertise on Instagram? Pew's got some data you should find quite interesting: Nearly half (43%) of cellphone owners age 18-29 use Instagram, but that percentage drops precipitously in the 30-49 bracket (18%) and 50-64 group (6%). Targeting millennials? Instagram away. Going for an older crowd? Look elsewhere." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAevcGFr5_-mkMIiJTignyygJaud5RB3E0fQn8_1dldRv2I3VbXw4X-TrJJQXiO2eF29y04818oR-MGbP5tWYBedou2hxr9knvG6XhiCSdMf2WnGMNjYfZNFgB1f3UfICtdnUR_rBLLmMzd6FVc0yxKeHQAPKHVyLuvdFOUVweKmw08WBJG3ERkCRDCs0EQ0jylgec5qOf455fQ==> .

 

Trending Tumblr Media

 

Marissa Mayer has declared 2014 the year Yahoo will make Tumblr more valuable, so Adweek's Garett Sloane looked at areas of opportunities for ads on the social site. Facebook and Twitter have paved the way for social advertising so the shock should be minimized to the ad-averse Tumblr user base. One big area Tumblr could open up is its trending section, and when it comes to paying for promoted space, companies would need better targeting capabilities, such as geotargeting. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAetLy5XJEyoiXE4MvqRGP2Kawn2zxvKVXXXoB5Chv57W1DmThoag-W7VPyOev8GHjej-0TVV1Dddsmu5BjZMUdG4l84w6G-4RZ9e7l5XJBIvg_B1K1uwzSUslZyW0zqx2KS6upVx3nOwAtmC-cdBl1FYNcI4-_PyvH6iH7ICaVSJsCKN1_7dOCK-kX27TVQmWqUi808-K0of7A==> .

 

Auto-Native

 

When companies began updating their technology to work with Facebook Exchange (FBX), it just so happened that these same companies were building capabilities for native to work with RTB, Ad Age's Alex Kantrowitz points out. Although native is the buzzword of the year, it doesn't mean publishers are willing to hand over editorial control of the content on their sites, and it doesn't mean advertisers are ready to take on the new format. Some native ad platforms, such as Nativo and Sharethrough, are working to standardize native ads in an effort to make RTB more effective. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAeuXntgieu79SMIbXura0TbNpjX0ifqGiUyR_L0H4H3-jwA5aHmOwEio0EkqICBsktEmTwZhJss_xsh6MlLXUhSAujCDTW4e45LFU4ggBwmWTG1r05Op8Ijq3482-AmT2dGb9BIlAfEWaIz-qS7U9UruYWA2tciUZbhXPcrqAy0hCw==> .

 

TV Measurement Everywhere

 

Nielsen is preparing its new SDK for measuring TV viewing through apps and other digital platforms, according to TechCrunch's Ingrid Lunden. Nielsen will be using portal companies, like Facebook, to measure who is watching the streams and where they are. "We've been working hard to deliver this new SDK and are excited to be able to deliver a single client solution that supports both the linear (TV style) and dynamic (Internet style) ad models," said Megan Clarken, EVP, global product leader, Nielsen, in a statement. "This unified encoding approach for video enables measurement to follow content across screens and ad models." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAev78AfTtOojRthMBYqyRB-hejYo0DK-yzHTZcsfvomcW5-ndjJh-Aty_x7-zNrRS2w7iYWIf0fFOhfbw8dbi2XbB2ixvW9WD4IAkxwaba-EhGlXCDuUne3XIIq2KiXzpMJ_2UXip5bTDuAoZW5drSb1PHs4T43almut9ymLi5eWMA==> .

 

Local Mobile Ad Tech

 

In a piece on Street Fight, BIA/Kelsey analyst Mike Boland looks at local mobile ad tech and sees the last mile to the cash register quickly getting addressed. He writes, "Besides customer service and loyalty, this has implications for the ad attribution topic at hand. It picks up where the steps (literally) in the 'path to purchase' end - the front door. If you think about it, attribution can't get much better than covering the un-tracked last few inches to the cash register. Offline ad attribution will be a term you'll start to hear a lot more." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0016AkXBt_hAeu2kQ45JM6e6OUsRUXLW2x3Iupv2oUWEHzKRiu2GBF__N87OB-3uoMufm82HjPBtaC2h42MNGlUMY34qQVSh5eTlT4wBblCjXTTAr2Ul_6pFn_N-2aO6Oy0vKoxzeXkOA1sllh3l5z-Ln-xc2sR71FSfJmycQmkTqlRwAO4UN4dxf6ggv5WK599mQb0lrbbE0pK2aEWsceJGaOgRjTdXTgK> .

International DSP Revenue

 

Due to regulatory requirements, publicly traded Safeguard Scientifics shares a few tidbits on the state of its investments on a quarterly basis -- this includes its investment in US creative ad-tech firm Spongecell and ad platform MediaMath. Beyond trumpeting the payday potential signaled by Rocket Fuel's IPO, Safeguard CEO Steve Zarrilli offered this about MediaMath during his company's earnings call last week: "From a network of 12 locations worldwide, MediaMath serves more than 3,500 clients and many of the top ad agencies. International operations are now responsible for approximately 35% of MediaMath's annual revenue. Safeguard has deployed $18.5 million of capital in MediaMath since July 2009 and has a 23% primary ownership position." Read more on Seeking Alpha (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPlnJD_cLaTHj1wv4r9AfRLHgv5pLnZAkUWLNODw1inQxMjkDAys9y0c5xz0-Pyqkz2qZ35PJqanoqVEM-3svKBhAOfo5SIvvmqys2WJJZMdYUApqDThU4kn6nSx8DNznGjZtppOfCx4vw2C0Jio2ZuNTIKLH3oxnwWiHluv7zF3QLGVSIQH8xix7aDZawNORyhNHQ6op9k9yAOJrIn0-OIgjFTNa7lUPJ3cKLAnzbFkKq5_0CAxbR1D> . And read the press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPmaqrJJjzT0QcZ4eyyHJ65H1-1jeTQGrDJMHzgVZ6mWoHBzfwbrdrLDFZYau1TBBomNUHr6V8fyrq0Qls6LFelaDbLHWeaKybALLH3Rx-1KLZRuoCVZ-2GdvM4Vpi3aLUE3EbXERMxkkoNAuBlxUfOw_GenicBNIJXOLY_WZ-_zdpVPFNiMRrCVi722t4QSI-vwPgsHH30PVkIrj-QmF01TfJp6ZWUB_8icpaciq6KBZlK9kLoFY9MlCoj-31re-v7Q1urBTc8HtZbTFb7rfxsB24VvrVo4CyLs1TafRPXp7DFvFh02DOG6> .

 

Auto-Play Delay

 

AllThingsD's Jason Del Rey says Facebook's plans to launch auto-play video ads are being delayed until 2014. He explains, "Facebook recognizes the risk of upsetting its user base with the ads, which are expected to play automatically (though audio will have to be turned on by the viewer), so it wants more time to evaluate how its users have interacted with similar noncommercial videos that it started to allow on its platform earlier this year." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPnoFwd_3SZfTVn1Xjan_YxIllcAQkiSaHLJCH__MiM8Q1n0RwY_UdEtQC_DuJjC_H9UVd5ErqIHcBFhBAlAVjl5zMfogeCaQ2nP3uTSZ5BPYluAFSxZaxTy512jXy4RZi5BAHdgXqeT_DpswUDDz0_YOXjVEma1XAT1C5FKS4ypyorNzFQhQjrd> .

 

Right Time, Wrong Message

 

Real-time marketing (RTM) may be becoming a requirement for brands, reasons Andrew Frank, research VP at Gartner, but that doesn't mean there aren't huge risks. Within recent big news moments, there is a growing list of RTM efforts gone wrong -- think American Apparel's "Sandy Sale" after the hurricane. Frank writes, "If you're not part of the conversation, you're not part of the community, so abstain at your peril. ...Unfortunately, because success gives the illusion of true spontaneity, it's become something that's both easy and tempting to imitate badly." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPlHNc8x0HsrfgLf3E_IZpV_8sT7snuJmAZx_wwpyi7x9UA1b_HnME1I8BnhMJPpCYDz_vT_sOOBPiJSGNkkHAOWUxeoDp0kw1tcE5U87ye_ApFeXXaDn5riUj7HQG7MsyWNjzMc7KtETgVJhWdKhkIb7wcEAX2V2ZLmSyS0wXg_4n6Nydnvl7dhI2gZ9-CoRGc=> .

 

Trading Media

 

Real-time bidding (RTB) draws many comparisons to the automated stock exchange. To that end, former Wall Street senior technologist Ted Yang and former Kantar CEO Bill Lederer are creating a new programmatic-focused advertising company called MediaCrossing. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPlAhtP_YHQYnzNv4yd7f2fEGmTVvudwbSrJx8S7TewfzF5Q8xaBbQMy27-N4_PqbzdPfKJCYNbflL4dkVjACGdgs--4UmIK9c27IwWuNvXYeFC3KLYq3AsM_1V7mC9yhourCH9auK19DqRXLBbxGr4-y5Ti-587QTYJgvz5n61PiUqwlxcJJbnBc57JL6UnPdTrqzH7JLeE2aSezaSYrpEfjvODbXZykww0tLmijOW_yZfc52j7WtNw9KyOW388_eQ=> . The boilerplate in the release hints at what the company believes is its differentiation: "Unlike other marketplace players, MediaCrossing may take principal positions on behalf of publishers, marketers and their agencies, thus assuming the risk of unsold inventory for the benefit of its partners."

 

Discount Mapping

 

In the commerce war, Google is slowly encroaching on Amazon territory and this time it's through integrating Google Offers with Maps, according to Wired's Marcus Wohlsen. Advertisers can now tag their stores with offers when a user is looking at a map, encouraging them to shop locally rather than going online to Amazon. Also, Google is offering same-day delivery in the San Francisco area, and if that offer is expanded to other cities it could be a matter of time before Amazon and Google compete directly for online commerce. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPkXj0QcRRJOQ45Q6jWFa60wFOa4uPqoqzyu4rLEiiHNMYcQDrn4KNF0XvqPBuqYpoE88-8B1zpVCqwred4gM9FmihQDEeGDRHlBsbmT3cQGkzlCTd88QK7YLPFNMyyKMcGYaokVb4gut_Tj50M88IJlMVXgY_ke2Ac=> .

Telecom Progeny Goes Native

 

Pinsight Media <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPlUgcNI2oW4Q_2xAL4MebnWhGW92SsbcHtVegRNinUmNj_GaLawOJlMhoToHSvVSAAdl3N7euJF_EtxuTqmt8UBYwSN-xmiFvq1UnkQR327qQ==> +, a Sprint-owned media company, is taking a stab at native advertising in a deal with mobile ad network Millennial Media. Pinsight Media+, which offers mobile ad targeting and app development, will display apps from Millennial Media's advertiser base as ad units that will appear on Sprint Android devices. "Consumers are always looking for their next favorite app, and we created these new products to blend advertising with utility," said Evan Conway, strategy and monetization VP at Pinsight Media+, in a statement. "The Millennial Media platform allows us to immediately scale these new units, and present consumers with relevant apps..." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPnNwztQcUzf-ZzHIV0v7LV7MHVaW6OwdV-B7IJPUSHtb_uSGSTK9aHdTKC7MAsQ0KTqqBVaq6maM7ijYmJvaLVVPebfhOOE0lhTBGrqe9THh8wyCsW-de013iSk0gkKhwazs_AnmstZLVrLeS2PN1ATtebecgKe9zQ3A26uk1MXnkA3U150sCi0RhyjdRVc4BHBkx2of9hyp5YlwF3BlsTXhA1wqR8AdGD1e2oW73U1_4LSnBmLXz99FqlEexgzjTGPYns5lVrVSHj6qYySPx5L82WaUkJ-lpSSgxfF9K0_aaYhfLbugwSQ> 

 

Cutting Out The Middlemen

 

Facebook's decision to offer its custom audiences tool outside of FBX could squeeze out some third-party buyers, according to Digiday's Jack Marshall. The fact that mobile inventory is only available through Facebook's API and not through FBX is another sign that the company prefers marketers come directly to it. "They're trying to scale their mobile native ad dominance," said Ross Sheingold, chief strategy officer at social media agency Laundry Service. "FBX isn't available on mobile, and shouldn't ever be. It isn't dynamic or creative enough." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010sQ0tE9YAPnJ8QvYibBzZ8gbBPyvXWW-hdfQJLyS9aS1oMV-YXlG5CuP7mOiWEKzEney_xJIrYPPL1EySDeTnllxGNYj8qqJrkU05W1tTlGx51SzSAuZZW6GLb-TvdYh0MMqaQOrDnGpTNtZcZKg92U3eXWK5HcmwG-lBGxIP7Q7ixJJj9N9GdTMIeqETqDp> .

Google Search Gets Display   



One could say that Google's Product Listing Ads initially brought <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD0qRo3aV1TWE4n72sYUgcdJFgv71VxOmEIiWyy3bRd2srZSkvBMPhTG77-qcYj5TKKoP22zGtkZgrjPBZA56VrQJ8A1d0cxGigokTSZCDmBNZebixFEgerkhqxzcRsANB3R3zEZXOktvAXbq4vQgKBI9HoG78ywO7zAilCkOo-id69L7X67kGlOJsEGsaQHe3o=>  the sweet nectar of display advertising to Google's search engine result pages (SERPs). Now, Google's showing nontraditional display ads for several select advertisers in the SERPs. The New York Times' Bits blogger, Claire Cain Miller, writes, "The ads are part of Google's multiyear evolution from showing text links to displaying a variety of videos, photos, company logos, maps and other visual information." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD3AiyBlvxNKcma-wlhCAuhjyqTLgom3wIPupV4-1t6l7IutOrj6AyTfXAeyLjbW_zTlCCMv7pW3yCVMJVM4yzhNksog19huJIU-ixwf8Aq4I23CCcWtEfuLctONW0COcyzKqkkkKOOzwjkZ_bU19sq7lJoBkDUtOwhd7RhqOTrusCIKQb6_LZlQ7jEnaGOl-ojlbVaVawJQTIDr1TgaGpYSHeWSiL0FN0A=> . Greg Sterling takes an additional look <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD0qEQrQjSskR19vUAAcu5P8DJvnoGiVp5-ecf-3G9-p3tlajXstgSvn7fhO_TfOGzatrMBAAOMNEjYgR0YchLmPk5B9lmxEgyzioJH1wGyyKYOHShZkQ5qPG3aAVxFr5Cc-YaPpYOhrWugkl2aWjaiS1lI77_e8UlwGcem20TghLUgnVyHHB4GPnWEeY6oVSlJgFsben4-MNEO2fRgUG9Ug>  at "brand image" ads.

  

Facebook Data, Instagram Ads

  

Facebook is opening up about its forthcoming ads on Instagram. Read the blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD3Sda0erfhOaljruJPUequZeijUd68fG7pafIFXATchfuJKSq6p_cs1fm3qqGWfzY1_kPXcieT62NSzACOFCy1JfrDb2ShuQfqnVPv4o9TxMiPTt3AI2T6XLxoMQu6I1ihj2bbYSalzeTQhIuiobruiy7Ucgd6gHQY=>  From the FAQ: "We ... will use information about what you do on Instagram and Facebook (our parent company). For instance, this might include the people you follow and the photos and videos you like on Instagram, and your interests and other basic info on Facebook." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD2WP6sm2F8bZxXXCZ6aKR73OThtNhcZz9ramRiSUKzT5y-rOVwzWTDbGnrdIvYcQc2jKW0sjWaJYbrg64RWsi0C6Rxmw3pWAjNxfDKoi5j0CMS_nPrmvqCM>  No word on whether Custom Audiences offline audience matching or retargeting will be offered.

  

Speed Testing

  

Real-time bidding (RTB) created fast, just-in-time buying of display ads, and now LifeStreet Media is bringing fast testing to the mix, according to VentureBeat. The platform, called RevJet, will be integrated with a number of ad exchanges including MoPub, AdMob and Nexage. "What we're doing differently is perpetual high-velocity testing," Mitchell Weisman, founder and chief executive of LifeStreet, said in an interview with VentureBeat. "RTB is a way of buying media, then there's a question of how you use the media, and how well you use the media." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD1Zgs9Gd5Mtubo4ZuZ6O6aY7RssY_w09yNYABS7N4rv4FVPpOWvrIa2Sy2TtWGIjl5z40eF9rosVf-hJXoVDpnSd8VtTGvOJlLcde_GK3rS2gL7M9IrLdggkTZ-lagBWl6cTLnewuqgxUQhYMTEUrd_A4SqkAdU1rqEedy3MsVFor1rodjmABsVb7QO0Z-jBvocH2-E0-E-bU8QbeRTL9huL99KgHk3KV0Oe9ss5AqAzA==> .

  

Twitter Worth Billions

  

As its IPO approaches, Wall Street's valuation of social (ad) platform Twitter is apparently around $11 billion. Read the S-1 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD3xwP0XH3IllbYsTwFihVVLOF5yiF1kQ6C9MzpL8-i9CkvuyL4pAXf2qo6e4CA2UeghNrY-mOZkZ0MRqvFA5wSQRyhuxNDeQkQi3Zedi4zh9Gaia5udXawSHZUOD_IQiF7IJMgh-PKuJgOsU7TtjOdsYn2c6epmKjavKu2lM9g720K-sx1sjUeOim1-isYnqSTZdhQgSZjnuw==> . TechCrunch runs the math: "[The] pricing indicates that Twitter could raise as much as $1.4 billion with this IPO or $1.6 billion, including the over-allotment option - which accounts for around a 13% stake in the company overall. Twitter notes that underwriters have an option to purchase 10,500,000 more shares if the IPO is exceeded at the IPO price less discount." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD0-1x-J6VgS3g1ROqJYW0fZcZnUWAajtrRi9H0DNy7EYKplSqO1qHLjzm-BoigRMYNYXDGj2fAopSJwYx1GgU5tPUKGfhvRWb_yid5BBHqRs34VTvD-rkcFTwGvn5dnWbnHEx2me-oiNfkhCZK5JeXU1Yxqr1xAplZFoXbdZFJGSCZ62xqIc6FN-51zQubVUqu9261F1PYSYKqPUkb57fvC>  So, Twitter will have about a billion and a half to buy stuff (tech) -- let alone the ability to use its valuable stock as currency.


WPP Earnings

 

WPP's Q3 earnings are in, and revenues are up 7.4% overall. Public relations and public affairs was one area with a loss of revenue, while advertising and media saw a growth of 8.2% in revenues. The company expects to see improvements in the Asia Pacific region as growth slows in the US, UK and Western Europe. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD3nWovtbqbCxJpYzZ43W58fxCUA9zaqzOvpKz318GmTXqsoLF2WdS8bXXyQywpq-Up8VqsiGQBdmmIHV9P0vazjAJ5GX8O6VxtzUbbbzG1JZc-JI5R-L2cTrZjaRcn8-MCec56e5x0CP7SJkcjz9KHMbGIWjJzUq1tkNmVw-6lHQbxif522jWVG0t-x9mx7yapSJ9fQkSlo9Q==>  (pdf).

Hail, Yield Chief

  

Viacom named John Halley, who has worked at the company since 2007, as EVP and COO of ad sales. Halley will be responsible for "the company's pricing and inventory, commercial operations, finance and business intelligence functions across the Viacom Media Networks ad sales linear and digital portfolio." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD39K2R7gdg7rcXrfCeO9Kvflk2ibfmetdUud_1KoYzkgPZwBGILaJS4UHmbxtBc8sE537146eRiCEtfINl4G3ZXpu97-N09GjvEVL42Cfy2kFRj3-ILPGzcvr-RZoXakoZi5xVGOB9CX4VN8KrOyucRPRvgMTTXOInMSVP6n-5qrC8apV9wUdJuW-ZAALQynf-YZkbjMA3jTVCkVXR7efBWPptEaJugZE5I9gwaUQxQZ4-jwh7OrJfoXakCqnC_dGOo0xKnhYYA62HNu2flSCClCTCP5KCbvrcspHB9w5hikoAkd8Q4lcvU> .

  

Data Matters

  

The Epoch Times is using Lotame as its DMP of choice to leverage all of its print and online data. The publication is known for its multilingual coverage of China. "If you don't have data, you don't have anything," said Amir Talai of Epoch Times. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD0m1WBEpbmvL4GwApdYYjDsvCt8vFwrtGynFWFsfEcle5ibN4NEH4zLWt-Yo7VtCWlf1OXUy6VUR5O-8f7JSdraSYwzXrZVOWITdGEuUferpziWxvp6s0yeSB9p7ULAXtW4b9Jd9UF4zmBMcBgl0_zqC_9CW24_Dtu54dp5C8PjDnuQPFqohKYW3GAnOItS4i85zH9v11riN8rWvnE-hm6Mm193a0pz2LI=> . Data driving media is language agnostic.

  

Perceptions: Marketers Vs. Consumers

  

A new study commissioned by ad platform [x+1] compares the differences between various marketing efforts and consumer preferences. The study found that 25% of consumers believe email to be the most valuable when making a purchase decision and only 2% found SMS helpful. Consumers' top three preferred methods of communication were email, a personalized Web experience and display, whereas marketers valued social over display. Despite the consumer preference for display ads, less than 40% of marketers include them in their media strategy. Read the report (Pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001MubLmS7RUD0VQ9_cggd5v8IJCGe2bLziIJoBAXhrZ5jT2FjCHUKJp8Pl1j0os6UBAh9FtCOObvYnnXP2KFMG1vcqpiBLDobamxEzXDH5_Qpl5pF4XxtyKrZxp1fL9PF75RVvuYu2bmgXnSd1-mPYNA==> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJEe9KTI-BlYYTjGauPZLuU5UBN5iwqtUBl_5C46jqk_9PKAJz0FlUvdCab4Gow9DGbp77Hd8szwgQSW9KU0-PJAL72jlRTdCXV3PDZ786sK-ppV6maHdpANgaVeYuK19p4=> .

 

Adelphic Dives Into Video

 

Mobile ad targeting firm Adelphic is adding mobile video inventory to its mobile ad platform, allowing agency and brand partners to buy and manage mobile video ads programmatically. VivaKi is one of the agencies that will be tapping into Adelphic's video inventory. "Except for the AOD video channel, we're not doing much with mobile video and Adelphic is getting us [the AOD mobile channel] off the ground in the video space," Jason Pope, VP of AOD Mobile at VivaKi, told AdExchanger. "Video is becoming a bigger piece of the pie and so the programmatic component is important." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJGJ7qlHZwXFP3slHks2tK7gOSesIFrtPorCQp06LuA_4iLwypdScAh5BVM8BY9Z030gZGhA_X1ZCdsdz7YrFfobofwafALPevQBs1tj_YVEFT_f_TsGOiK4zwec-0jHy2NmCk3qk8__qkIGLBcIaXQcAgNyGugVgmY=> 

 

TV On Twitter

 

Twitter is raking in the TV opportunities ahead of its impending IPO, and this time it's partnering with BBC to create in-tweet original programming and distribute via its paid-tweet Amplify program, according to Ad Age's Jeanine Poggi. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJERKoZrl92KsViJhptMX80O-KPewE1Jd0bJXYUagX34cce9FHDZOhU7uIPpJS87VTz014ZXQUDaxcmvX5lx5nqRrz7hkfsF8hdbcze-x4iMzNWyLMay6NckDZ8Ws9V5wPC6okyg8j9zCr2JhgMZ-sp1MWmL6cRxfCQRXcGaW25D6g==> . The Amplify program has been used for in-tweet video content from Viacom, CBS and Comcast in the past -- but that was for existing TV programming. Original, Twitter-only video programming is a first.

 

Subscription Yield

 

YouTube is opening up its paid subscription option to more creators. GigaOM's Laura Hazard Owen is reporting that as long as the channel has more than 10,000 subscribers and has AdSense linked to its account, it can use the paid subscription functionality. So far the biggest partners are outsiders, such as National Geographic Kids and Sesame Street, but the loosened criteria should open up the paid option to insiders. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJEBo3C0aX4KbdBYecInmfeyAj16TDGq74fpKOdqFBp1kG2UcjeLOEsK1goSr0KlgqFETLK1P5KDEFnts6jwU4tt_UurWNE0Er_XWDWA1cQBgu1b4-JPJsgi32jwXejEBnRnoxV1QZ24UMsuUOYGFTzWoDHCd2F3At3be5IjDuE0_STGYEfWcnNGAmH3B6KhkrnAYlDK-gaxDg==> . The yield dial of the future includes content+commerce+ads.

 

Coffee's Feedback Loop

 

Marketing can pour itself another cup of big data at Starbucks. Reuters reports, "Over the next year, Starbucks said it plans to double the number of its Clover coffee-brewing machines, which connect to the cloud and track customer preferences, allow recipes to be digitally updated and help staffers remotely monitor a coffee maker's performance." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJHZaK-atguRIICVIfegjSck6GEWmjcloX7l0gml0lsyIEMcsF0EOA61dWqcEc-DpyWtj1ec86uxLwKan_-mUu7U1OkAqd6Sh94XsmpTpwU6XjdunY4Sa8Ljse9ov4FYJkYw7TJc_va-I2PzlnBIKLJxFzwu__ym6xNLCWIJwgf5ELvJZrs1mGMzqajEI_2IBNb9c969z-zGsrXW8g6wF1jC> .

 

Business Everywhere

 

Facebook isn't the only one with stellar mobile numbers. LinkedIn is also realizing the importance of users on the go. Mobile now accounts for 38% of unique visitors, and users who use both desktop and mobile are 2.5 times more active. The company also announced an update to its iPad app, and a new feature called LinkedIn Intro, which provides key information for a user within an email. Read the blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJHeQJr5VpMbE1PZLMHHGB9hsqmrh--2e1ZHiYORxG91T7Weu_Xu5RmotpC3WRtWpDMWRhSjRSOy3UeMndSA20t8Vsv7WKzvnm3kcP-tJl9plmTQBiRJTfirRJnLWi1-ZCRlRZ7NGjpzRPau-jJKrlcGmTiCflleoCFEBaEJdjWrnTNAgF7YYqm8gVNput6jLCNbBYJQccWZFtIGkOabw_to> .

The Persistent Discrepancy

 

The IAB's Joe Lazlo outlines the complications of ad ops, especially in mobile, in a column for ClickZ. One of the biggest difficulties is discrepancies in counting ads, both on the agency and publisher sides. He writes, "Understanding mobile discrepancies and establishing lines of communications to address them are key steps for the maturation of mobile advertising, but the mobile ad ops plate is very full beyond that. Making sure that ad creative will actually work on mobile devices and handling the issues that arise as the not-yet-standardized mobile world moves to enable programmatic buying are also big challenges." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019GbdtAfwOJF1_FGCcdisEaCG7ls_2hxx9YxTgOCE2NyO7--rwY603EDxEMR3Sjw1QsqQN05Fhrc_9-xx1jtrmMoI1FpqhZMhMgfywQ_BjPkR2G2MkFxqnZtbCU6ceMZ88FP5dUxJGHTGejvHqt4o8CnMZdrsBX6v_AQKHlaba26iDseHjpMAsQiohVRhuUqcPeP-BEsGVRvgp3gwFdcmnJUUL2pNyPatBlOTCy0UTxP_ZleUafCc05eCDT_0u-D2> .

Purchase Data In The TV Buy

 

Simulmedia has added consumer purchase data from Nielsen Buyer Insights to its non-primetime TV ad-buying platform, MediaPost reports. CEO Dave Morgan says, "Having these databases is not new. But they have always been used for research purposes. No one has ever activated them." The company collects data from users' set-top boxes, and now works with TiVo Research and Analytics, along with Nielsen. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMj8NP8l9F1i23GDOyDxb3w5sAOTBUW8sKDAbsrP6zkI2lrnbv_FBTmsocSZRK1pUiCN8H_FL9w2VIKFseKA5kDnVM1Z1E8-kwxwlPLEYpekS_xUHJgeiQn0BITiycFfyfpuQRitS5USxkUSmzm7cfkxgQkcJRBZj5ya2y72FH1QoA-LheBzuxebyMGP9Nm6ymbS__BmdH-Nl_LW7bWArTN7pP3cLOIikQSEc55Y5Mv6piCLT6vwj9riT96RLJYG_q4=> .

 

Search Tension

 

The epic partnership between Microsoft and Yahoo, created to regain some search ground lost to Google, has become strained, according to Reuters' Alexei Oreskovic and Dan Levine. The two companies made a deal to expand their partnership into 16 different markets, 14 of which have already been implemented. After Steve Ballmer announced his resignation, Marissa Mayer wanted to wait for the new CEO to prove his commitment to the deal before finishing the transition in the last two markets. U.S. District Judge Robert Patterson Jr. and an arbitrator ruled in favor of Microsoft. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMixPNJlNoZWE5lI9Zm_ptcn_mrK7SnmgD9y0mNv16tB454lPy_AkyYKdZZ6r_Nd5r7ehH9zlbWP0gnvZBdNAjMGKAVwe4kA-hWQUB6kU7v6oicLt6NLEeGy5bNRZgDdtwK4r47ch29R4-5Rh40foiRsE2li81jkgGPPyGZyk2pYWctpxlwOteExSSa8BRNNm6RFxTsGwc0Ubg==> .

 

Boston Tech

 

Ad-tech M&A is gaining velocity, so Boston Business Journal's Kyle Alspach compiled a list of six ad-tech companies in Boston that make good acquisition candidates. His list includes DataXu, OwnerIQ, Visible Measures, Nexage, Nanigans and ChoiceStream. Alspach also gives an explanation for each pick. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMgF-Z9aDzxrBEvoXyCeNalGVMr2Kxv-CmpCWMZVOqxLXOfM6TJ8NjoS_kJbnDgiO1yZEHe8Y-2nFpKxc0jTsKN9yYJw5QazlIfMSrSMudvfAUTKKGNAh4j0Cjdi0mtRMKEAd6I8glVuUfCg-gGjrC2xfi-4F_3J1t9elzl9jiNS7PdnJsGkbvbUWT6HEhxTzv4t8IkILrD79b3Uy8l8lmuHsQCjPY4VYQnIOl9ChXOuyS3-9h8mvGSO> .

 

Ad Spend Trends

 

In its Global Ad Spend report, Nielsen finds ad-spend trends continue to favor TV and display, at the expense of more traditional media such as radio and print. TV now accounts for 57.6% of total ad spend. Display ad spending is up 26.6% from last year, thanks in part to growth in the Asia Pacific region and Latin America. Outdoor ad spend grew in all areas by 5%, although it's still a small piece of the pie, like display. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMgrvDrvuqd51GczyXHu2GE_qNRSe2c11rZrx5OFyWuLdwvqSuv6EA3XlrTYyQ6fFiGMVzEFLWZL1HuZwpsHbWnIL2xZ0DuC1kuh5xqNwMMsAc65WdtAjwjyYDRbzebpaHsIPd-VhDj-VmF2EveiP1lKG_gMg7yAM2HV-nPz7eQsxiI-oak1jN7caeFHc11J_JkPSEkCUsdESDMQJCHHBoGoemN2So8oYnV2dvjDGN25tg==> .

 

Branding Study

 

Forbes and IPG Media Lab partnered up to conduct a study concerning the effectiveness of long-form branded content. The study involved 2,259 participants including Chrysler, Woodford Reserve and Charles Schwab. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMjthQcccBvW8BfvlbfHQOvcohdRqOP3HAzHw3kl5da3IAYneAHcMuu2MMtp7-y8ehHsxjRZFfrghiHumf8gtJbWTCkh0_KFz5saikj-z39zbyW62GTmAKZ57P-u7jzykcMIpCouTAbPfmZyPPRxB17pqe1efwTzsDQ0bn2KZuyaaDVEDFiGQZHSugYtApfZRVg=> , read the report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMgEpyrc8kkepHOylJ0mQbRa8t4DGqmUtmWV9WIZMOgP7NQp17C08huaBKDmZwOtCmdChQNctryudXsmnNw17D3HaOTQgg7S2y2m5aHcaUxGELvS0cX-hj6KMTWxeRtRTESe77P2aGEZGFsqogOttzcpgGdk6-RRzsLWhGxNNCoupE-W3Io4jlChUd_tzWs0iKYVAz2yRtuqz9x1zEL7Lae4>  (pdf).

Making Apps Stick

 

App retention should be top of mind for developers, Gartner's Jennifer Polk writes in a blog post. As with loyalty programs in stores, apps should provide a service or functionality that a user can't get anywhere else. Polk writes, "I don't have the space in my phone to hold on to apps that don't serve a purpose, not if it requires me to remove valuable media or prevents me from getting the latest update. I don't have the time to thumb through five or six screens to find the app the I need or try in vain to use an app that has bugs." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMgT7X4KWjsE18i0Pj4ozThCBOcrI4Guhs7mmLE_BeDbp-NiRuxTxESq2fH1WSM7sIFI4vytbZCbIBjuo-FrYWMf0ZndnZeGtjLPm9G6ohOOGVU40lS5Djx_Ywgm86-boAgTfzZQ195c5AXvkhumkWTA53S-jiCJM4rH4znDGaG9U7upe6LpsO6WdZ8ProHxAEA=> .

 

Trading Up

 

Multi Channel Network is moving ahead with its automated trading platform, which it hopes to have done in 2014, according to AdNews' Frank Chung. CEO Anthony Fitzgerald warns against the diminishing returns inherent in over-targeting. "There will be different systems that will trade inventory in whichever way they [the networks] choose to trade, but what will happen is the industry will build a hub between the different systems that will help automate the whole process at their end." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010B4YMG7VLMheZrvHCpPqhsXCTMSTyYQrwJI28cQ8F3GiOBm1nkAUZeh0PZzVJkTfcZYxLko2sv9VvoDIKHnpH0pnY5z9gF_iT2NRowNVw8FtEw08NnAqJwyCLmi4Vf08dnJmBS0bcNZol4GDxM9kFo3v7FDwzp27NCS6oaj7ToiFXCrspMFcGfsORu4RbXeF5uChbyqcnWoYz5OAfWt5bMIwYHpUsTPb> .

Prepping For The Holiday Lag

 

Holiday shopping and spending is projected to decrease again this year, according to The New York Times' Stuart Elliott, so some stores are ramping up efforts to gain foot traffic. Two examples are Premium Outlets in Roseland, NJ, and Toys R Us, which are hoping that running ad campaigns earlier and offering shoppers more flexible hours and more frequent deals will boost sales this season. The companies are also making social media a bigger part of their campaigns, and Premium Outlets plans to implement flash sales. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVYp9SGp4x3dV14rCQzESTE8wPsVqwKu9n-fEfQnSyqgL09QQT2-ipOCTGQi7WmBncTYUp2qIquZqfE7wyqCPMKPESkl0AarqOJ5owCY0UF56vASUt99VKeLMUvftVFD4J04AIMGnDP14CrfsG9B6X4CfFMiloGRFwrs4jy-va-8NlQc7OvY6z1WbXosUk5205U9nXWy-YZ1MFI-B2rWJEZD3K6OmrAjL7fUIXs_qzxOXw70-d-TrX8-OnNyF3moi38=> . Programmatic opportunity, too?

 

Facebook Ad Updates (Again)

 

Facebook is on a roll with ad updates, this time with a new method for buying mobile app ads. Now, businesses can bid on cost per action (CPA), which Facebook claims is more cost effective than CPC bidding. The company also announced the ability to use video in news feeds to promote app installs, allowing potential customers to watch a video about the app before installing. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVYVaiFdR9UzAvq2cyXKlcP6jhTXl1UKXrqSJMJUd-ZQ0Ge6RRvMj681n9-8XDkjPsm13MFIDMDJ36vOyF79R6BtLEyzxS7DtVabZTkud2MTy6hV31Kd7U1SvFEM3gpm0hafqgA593PFqtpAgr8G5AE1-9_eHOgsJaZ1pySivEJ7ak_LN1YQLFDahCKfQeZf_9FgcorWhkSPgIYC0yUQZx7SviSfXmzmOHk=> . Facebook is also cozying up to publishers by offering a new  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVb9Krbvi_6U3L0vF6rpw2vsKnLPBFoKv7Xoh0XvspTUd4yrz6NZpK6nnNHEWKPYoMWpEl9vftDIvowTh8TLIfpt-jMjE4iDd8UoPObG851CiA2ALuqQGljCN5XcnbiFdoz9dmYKANTHk3nwZAfCCYwA-rXxn4-RwS5oasfTWAaMdSjqigAtTmbcHvAZ87tJzOKO4GthM1kb6NSBWr_csNvzfT5PMkxCFrpLwYsIvA7DOPCdTN1-QNwX> "Stories to Share" feature on media pages. The new feature will give publishers a glimpse at what they haven't shared from their website yet, along with a button to do so directly from their Facebook page.

 

Creative Tech

 

PandoDaily highlights the competition created by the launch of Google's new "Ready Image Ads <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVbBMZ_9CpG9wcEItkS48ioy_2z3EwWY58ZOG12UAqbUdTtaaF5Fou2a2Wc6NgFC5P7QrgC28ZID3_aJ5GsOd0fDCG7LINej1Gn2vnFKgUVNYoXYVQ-JCAUI7fgjJ9NQLDL0I6vQqRHQvsIJWVmuKhS0JqRpnUuKzUEPWhLTrMdWxsz0tJJhXL-prCR4EgnMzzQ=> " to display ad-tech firm PaperG. PaperG's co-founder, Peter Lee, tells Pando, "We've seen a trend of companies realizing that creative is the major barrier to display advertising. Google entering the space is a testament to the growing strategic importance of ad creation, since it's the starting point for all ad campaigns and where the dollars flow." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVYbWtOV4kV1gLvA8tTFQZtqdjlHWYeJqlcHasjSWqI2fsHaT3wi1ixTJulbZ1lwnf14LqmiW1xH0YSL6ljAIciRoGfos9cUh6ypf2OEQ5b3Bv6Ym7dy_QzDSkWL8BDMNYk-aTzj0ByZmF_TKnGv-75HBkut1rOhGqz4I3hqMipzQkil9Mve4_vo7KVHkYjwaolp7tgxk5aYs29mXLhzumhao-XETJdEuys=> .

 

Re-couponing

 

Coupons are regaining traction and going mobile, according to revised numbers from eMarketer. The original projection for the number of people who will redeem coupons was 4.6%, but the new number is 11%. Tablets are also being included for the first time, given that shopping is one of the most popular activities for tablet users. From the article: "We expect ... one-third of all smartphone users ages 18 and older, or 42.1 million people, to use a coupon obtained via app, mobile internet, mobile barcode or SMS this year." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVYZit2a7Xj8-OioTgiZe5J9A2eu1D8F7GaIXVOS9lfmupR2RPSgpCQlXVIJf1iD06tSrX7YLccy8DcfHrsSgdggTWSed-LDh3Fr-JS3ZczycxVNqITDiIX7YxG2VtdTMn1uhFu8_kODam2IihxfDZP-G-8bo47UsOhbOX_vp1uTc351IicJDTm_rxZIrKmUFNG5JvMFfaJosC7zPt_sNbuBjyzpWKWoF1Q=> .

 

Ratings Online

 

With measurement firm Nielsen's Q3 earnings report coming on Wednesday <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVY78Fd0F_A8BBcqMU3keLjZMjKsoadr8-k34u9sawXurbqAZir45X1ODvyFjTlhsKeg5LgMju2q4Xsico1Io0faZoYChw2uMEfrp3BXpWyuutlavm5xSynLokXtDaPDO9mknUP2SeQ-LwJoKJiPh38S4M-Z3BWRibo=> , Pivotal Research analyst Brian Wieser takes a look at the measurement firm's Online Campaign Ratings (OCR) product, which aspires to bringing TV budget online. Wieser says there's traction, BUT: "Issues limiting OCR include absence on Google's YouTube, the absence of Facebook data on children under the age of 13 -- reducing the perceived quality of measurement on kids' Web properties -- and challenges integrating online and offline measurement given the differences in the composition of the panels used today."

The Tablet Grail

 

Magazine publishers may have hoped tablets would be the cure for their digital age woes, but Adweek's Lucia Moses reports some bleak statistics about tablet use from the Magazine Publishers Association. Aggregated news apps are a growing trend, and now 97% of those apps are free, meaning people aren't spending time in any one magazine app. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVZjgCKQeEVEE1x3NrO-MMnQFOaze734pbfeNN2lKrK2Q9-tJiH7Y1Y_NHv7LlKLEcDQ4-3X6fsbCkZldZjzjlIrpLkKksGkXHw8IvP4aKTFlnhyiOIngxCVZjpJXIJGOkvVHnz1bdfQwoeffpSdjM_RLB-SmtmHyM8p6OQWr9K9sNbO5q_SyaXI> .

 

Mobile Analytics

 

Yandex is bringing its free Web analytics tool to mobile, the company announced. The product, called Yandex.Metrica for Apps, creates customized reports, provides real-time information, offers crash reports and will work on any platform. The company is also working on a complementary marketing tool, which will give developers data such as traffic sources and funnels. Read.the.release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Zifhkt2yUVZbYFMq8PC9mNgYjFuBprJUoNlu_Im3QhMs6isNK_cB2OCNZGxPWnUfBezkVSBuMJHcSEcV6LLUNtM8U8Nk2AUuQSw8blE2wYZ8MQRxBM69m4IWjVKiZneAtDUfziWoCY9itM3PRnjEsNJqGftSpJUkdtctQ5ZV0Ap8o0RC97z-DGzA6PK2xtIf49kKSLw-vwg=> .

Microsoft Talks Ads

 

Microsoft delivered a Friday update on its latest advertising initiatives. The timing may speak to the lack of compelling news. In a blog post, there's no mention of programmatic or real-time bidding (RTB). But, if you're a behavioral advertising believer, you'll be happy to note that when buying Microsoft site inventory through Microsoft you will get some new behavioral targeting features. Windows 8 app audience gets a mention as do some new ad formats. Read it now <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpdTVxGJV9lgHvNKA43Tiyq_PXKRENJ6uGon1lTHG7_VbHD2IPWKTL_eRs3XnJQltFwABwJMHMuBwvcLOL-iXFxA3aHyxLi6Boy7Ikn34QlwDvv1GUmrXZMfbDv0U9on4nuvcPQKCWvJFBS11rObEGQcu3Q_NdXFuoYR1j-LGRC0SnLF4N-WPkyy3dcGzUEcFMng9oxULieXRSKMD3446U9wZuikBj_wW6UdweOW5yDF56u-O8l9ylCAbkfP-12139UeW2ZVeegF1g==> .

 

Real-Time Data

 

Casale has released buying trend data for its Index SSP (sell-side platform) covering the first half of 2013. Get it here (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpcTwsLHXs3MFtDRdbNpvsnQ2aUtsVSfcHz9HnewpPyrBT0c0_ywq_81rE5jz3kIoOJEfMkJxiNqAm1BJmUVF81gO9beT5VJmevwcHCZPVxbAoHe_G-QpYpKIAe0uNJfYrDXLyQDZPaiPvsO3y8HiGl_q6MZx2nb0ElraChlt7zQuPxIuMS5qyD6> . Among the highlights: "The top five DSPs still account for a large majority of marketplace spending (70%), with the top three accounting for just over 50% in Q1 and 42% in Q2." More in Adweek <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpeT8iTKiF508HsjYqJcEDRQNrZQ7VpFR5ohoBGYJXEBhN64FZ6tFJ-rZLZEp1-RqjBzy8Y5LdoKnDV7GnbMFbPIr_mipLo7uGbeFOeYcX4hK7bVlQ2u5Gq8HqvyTANYAxz20XIB7b1iE86BoEAOUh2TEbznnt6ztSuwL7aZXpubDtmGGOcru7QuKAae3KBOrq-hwb1ayegQEC4-4GcHlGsD> .

Google wins by a mile this past September, say the Evidon tea leaves. More in Ad Age. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpetmIR3KkGyIwFZLhmcmdykT2_AgLowWRTMg3J0hThvLVxN40GdQfudlEfzcS4W1ZbyMnngvz4hSl1eDaVPDpI6d7mGjLtj0zCllZwgOp7CcOGVxqzNmCJHElWjisSTw_jtGR9yHx7LVCJXFbcwKyMUzpPk0YtN5F0qmoYavGunzw==> 

 

Tech Wealth Saves News?

 

eBay founder Pierre Omidyar has announced that he'll invest $250 million in a new news site led by journalist Glenn Greenwald among others. This comes weeks after Amazon founder Jeff Bezos spent $250 million to buy The Washington Post. In reviewing the investment trend, The NY Times media writer David Carr reaches out to his Times colleague and exec Michael Zimbalist, who says, "(...) successful mid-career entrepreneurs are investing and willing to play the long game. They have been disrupters themselves and won't be bringing the same assumptions to the table." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpcywjy-J677jCkCWwMH066IPRWBhVOv_I7k0fiX0eYs4sVV54r4JEj0p7-67rglC-U_YtYx3TpbyKskXlXtxf6ugtsQ_eSaOU8ZPlrC-8-1m6pPF7WTc6JWrWaAz2z6FeLAs4eYnd6B_-tb-q_BjdnMhUSMBCkdl5YWreUhCLvFyoTzPj1uvNWqSmVygzoMpZYXPIQ3rE2V6d3LOVRYowq_cJQsImhC-Ew=> .

 

Amazon Threat

 

Paypal's biggest competitive threat may actually be Amazon, according to CNET's Donna Tam. The ecommerce giant has amassed a lot of payment information and built a trusted platform that could give it a leg up with its newest "Login and Pay with Amazon" initiative. Other companies, such as Google and Facebook, have tried to break into the payment space, but so far their efforts haven't gained a lot of traction. "I think Amazon is one of the handful of companies that can be a threat," said Patrick Salyer, CEO of Gigya. "There's the brand and trust associated with Amazon. ... We think they have a pretty good shot." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpcvavYls5MkANr8qaeljjhXt94O7T519jOR8FKQErhOM066N7i6QxyAIpVoGY0GhNbk9AFzmsVRzBkXSccBfAU6juWBCc4CImbL1fm0oUPCGhsK-OBZCQTNBAJHs9bHMZOXuUnum0UlwhynqcBK7WCsIfmtrMOY_hFWHC8k6OQMlMlH7EcdlqtMaskbP3CoUGjbvNeG7rVG5g==> .

 

Scaling Native

 

Laney Whitcanack, chief community officer at Federated Media, thinks the best way to scale native advertising is through programmatic efforts, which she outlines in a column for ClickZ. By using pixels and tracking users, advertisers can reach users with native messages wherever they are on the Web, much like other forms of display ads. She writes, "As an industry, we need a platform that combines the data-based and automated characteristics of programmatic buying with the custom, high engagement aspects of content marketing. This will allow distribution of content to the right people, at the right time, in the right context, at scale." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jxtmHcTaxpclt9evpqILmL9KMz1H1ERt-O5HNscnWrfnPT8tFO-1XeElfgaE5ImQCRzxTUi-M_cQRkFc594yMz8usaDEjmpVkLDXBjzk79erAYiWLA4uSXYYnSGvhGxKYS_XozGyGM2WliwR8N7KYeRWqXcb5VzdruuhJoo3WJI7QZwgD6xvENkqeVvQCVme7vEJ_ccUMXMZXlC4bphS1g==> .

Expanding Second Screen

 

Targeting the tablet? You'd better be, says Pew Research in a new report that shows affluent audience is expanding on the second screen. From Pew: "Up from 25% last year, more than half of those in households earning $75,000 or more now have tablets. Up from 19% last year, 38% of those in upper-income households now have e-readers." Data Confusion

 

Marc Guldimann, co-founder and CEO of Enliken, makes the case for why behavioral advertising is different from information collected by the government for surveillance purposes. In a column for Quartz, Guldimann points out that the types of information and methods are extremely different between the two, with advertisers collecting far less sensitive data. Advertisers use data to make ads more efficient and relevant, while government organizations collect data to track citizens to prevent, or solve, crimes. Guldimann also says data collected for advertising doesn't help the government in its own collection process. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qDLXnS5aCH3CqAzHFiyEz0bPLb6NvJ_nbx7yZ9CPpr0EBECEY6Gsul1giQbjLlDqNycqvsR1o9UtNKVfhh3GmRd5DfktZyXrNgkCkmH7uRIlql1jNI2XaRTuXuyu6m2p6HsSbluCjFHkQ8yB7ECrYqpnBEEExZy9zYXRFfhTowza-0Cjvh2HKBYLrMb_6NaVDzaKZfm9Gr22lv5aGUdu2g==> .

 

Programmatic Brander

 

Bob Arnold has left Kellogg Co. for Google, according to Ad Age. Arnold will work in a newly created position, which will have him running Google's ad strategy in North America for in-house brands. His wife will go from Kellogg to Google, too. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qDLXnS5aCH0Ts4QOw0ObTKjFFQ9pWnekrDpSEzU7cuY5C5FYKYKpdQKxnUrpmoxZeuSaBvs5yIkDRF8g_oWuz63yEe7dqfJWi-OYaOO65frbmr-7oAAsmumimZ8u1K_U4UZTp880aYKbKwXl6TF_v2nt-CrUZ31FooE3CbRRHjKM6Q2SS59yeTUBcXLfUKvGRd2JiGRVliZjvRhFw7INGQ==> . Maybe Google has something in store on the brand side as it relates to programmatic media? Arnold could be the pitch man.

 

Data-Driven Email

 

Marketo has announced an update to its email product called Dialog Edition, which attempts to lure customers from so-called "traditional" email providers. The idea is to capture user data and tailor emails in real time, and to use data across multiple platforms to ensure unique and pertinent marketing messages. Sharp Electronics marketer Dan Wynne makes an appearance in the release: "We moved to Marketo because it provided all of the email capabilities we required, plus the ability to automate and personalize our conversations with prospects and customers across all digital channels, resulting in higher opens, clicks and revenue." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qDLXnS5aCH0DEYijfMo22KFBpZjn-vLvYVV2EuVH2PUd4yRB8KHRhrhjMiUJbIoFlm3Y43wGm1EiypOops8zYn73c6umaPP2ksEmjqx7gj38jsS2htssi5Vtijrd4xQkPQdAM7U-ZJIzyt3-K5SyUYbsQA90kyjrikTygeooYFkmKypjUv9trTxB1NcnixTwkqGyh4l8pLtZjskZXHk-o9mv6NQ-WSpzVB3EXBexOYrhITaEG1u9tWJt0Xy5XgDaxvfAsfCN7qzfkrW9NUTlhQ==> . At what point is Marketo programmatic instead of automated? Splitting hairs?

 

The O'Kelley Way

 

Brian O'Kelley lets The New York Times' Adam Bryant look into his CEO "hat" in an interview about how he leads real-time ad platform AppNexus. The key to running a great company, according to O'Kelley, is to always be teaching and learning. He also employs a policy of transparency, allowing staff to email questions that then receive honest answers. Read the interview here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qDLXnS5aCH0hLDRjEq3tSyn5Y7bpHFKCSfu3wfk6UpHMdFpVSUl7dTPqMC5SiWp6d6_Uvkwmd2vA7qS4CdsCMgqwtGPwyJqfZi8cQCqCTnndrsqNV2CjsHdRA8jiYbZSaznCfU2N8kP0TFDznkeZKpNIYP74MkwTSeVCZT6mwUPAk01-eaKJFdRBS77FKvOHWntcrk0Rg33hHPAm5U6vh2TdNe1b81c_8DeBi652Q9WCtlwQpwZWq87ekLcXQJFoK16_XTpJmewvjxa9g4LU9xYKTRgQzaXIdPDIN8f73-k356TKaC3W2w==> .

Dispop says in a release that it has created an impression-based, self-serve buying platform for the little guy (SMBs). The word "programmatic" makes it into the release: "Dispop integrates with all the major programmatic ad exchanges like: AppNexus, OpenX, Rubicon, Pubmatic, BrightRoll, Google as well as Facebook Exchange (FBX) for both direct targeting and retargeting capabilities through a single dashboard." Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qDLXnS5aCH3c9d-RGsmQCYP-Sv4frvPtBT92OuE_tljzISzSLu8gksSQnU4QqV792vsB5W8fDqNa2XyvfRvMAfu5ZdYpbfFIoHcx3Nn5N29B3Wyi3QbiitA03TkVPakhkRJL5iv5ah-ltjy7DlbZBLslextPZvpRtjStQNSU5b3jjX88ikciz5eQicv__BZwK3_boXtAh6TZku59np2mIaJM92ozVTqSQr1y3yP4pEg=> .

Mondel?z Targeting Offline

 

Impulse snack buys are a data opportunity for Mondel?z <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZP3hy8PNu8bmdcMBy5PHHmPMqkiegTyFf95LX0J51rcCCpYZW8fJO9yvLoN8Ba7GddXTy3fbs1y8h72SKp1FCodCB2ZZKoFmZ26QLwRTFOiaiS6iH9DAK7vAaHZMBpyYNtTZgyHNyKyspea8Fv0M_ClXrbPR_Oz6>  International, which is working on "smart shelves" that will use sensors to gather basic information, such as age and gender. The Raw Story's Travis Gettys reports that information could be used to serve targeted ads and coupons depending on how long people linger and what types of snacks they pick up. According to CIO Mark Dajani, the sensors won't collect photos, videos or other personal information. "When people walk by, it's a missed opportunity," Dajani said. "We must know how the consumer behaves in the store." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZP3hy8PNu8ahpCXDsSlAqxA61ZCB84-HCa6799nIOw850TB7BPEYuunuMXUIi8RZQKRweovAgEh-d27ZHWD80151H0SqBpQUxd7_qMd6rvykLbjv8T0PsMXKeIRDZtqiMVYEfkBil4lJQ0BZAMrP3L8kXLgJbwi-DrtBBOIY9ovz13I1Bzr1mE2JPn9A3tiRgiB6N59dW-NCFoid2qUv2bBwu1LQbpH2_nP-e3kvi9lKwQhqw1BJxh_eq7GcHMT07k1Or8Vr7hA=> .

 

Pass The Tech

 

Doug Weaver looks at agencies and ad tech in a post on his company's blog. He says agencies have made some mistakes in implementing new, automated technologies. But, he thinks someone inevitably had to take the lead given the complex nature of advertising technology. He writes, "It's possible that no matter how the agency holding companies (creators and sustainers of the main trading desks) handled themselves, the current dynamic would have played out anyway: digital technology always ends up disempowering the middlemen." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZP3hy8PNu8ZO7-VyZJyWHzVMskGaEyftqFbySF15MyQ8e5GGA1dBg5g7RUxzxVmHjB7m3DpQdAXkMz6GEpaYtJ4BUU7p8sYLuJxJ9Rp1__fT2VkSycdTSZ9hlZI9N83zRlox4tBaOrRvi6sfQFviVyfBgMo0qIe2> .

 

Akamai On The Internet

 

Akamai released its Q2 2013 State of The Internet report detailing the traffic it saw running across its IP-based content-delivery network. Among the highlights: "Year-over-year, average connection speeds were up 9.2%, with nine of the top 10 countries/regions demonstrating positive growth of more than 10%. Worldwide, 127 qualifying countries/regions saw a year-over-year increase in average connection speeds..." Tracking In-Store

 

Nomi, an in-store analytics firm, raised $10 million in a Series A round of funding, according to Mashable's Lauren Indvik. Nomi tracks users' mobile devices to see how long they were in a store, the type of device they were using and the percentage of users who walked by a store and went in. Although the company hasn't given any client names, CEO and co-founder Marc Ferrentino says they are working with some "pretty substantial" retailers and restaurant chains. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZP3hy8PNu8YF84wlahWes7xbCrGZOnsyiyoHi75-2YMVMZEOOafl1TzeqRoFrMBqy6gxSACKdcRK8aewNN52gbQRzWR08X0pbNEHGna0RFZVvoKHpQS8juK9Q6o_YFlMD4r1Z_PJRBkbVqZ5N6KogHuz7YXEL45y> .

 

eBay Q3 Earnings Snapshot

 

eBay posted net earnings <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZP3hy8PNu8aoGv8PJW_hdorQEqZ3xVSX992L3a_XvBXE6vklM3OhV97zwOX-6bmlUkzxijb4moLNLQYlslGiRDiAA0Xx5VhKYWgcpwRoUzxwMG822Rq-IlqLp0K7Vlw1HldTme1c4jQFldokLYy6RoU07MLJi1j8dzCNMXbmXbGlnIXcI07RRA==>  of $3.9 billion for the third quarter, up 14% year-over-year; net income was $689 million. In a breakdown of business units, payments, unsurprisingly, saw a strong growth with net revenues that totaled $1.6 billion, a 19% increase from Q3 2012. eBay's PayPal acquired payments platform Braintree for $800 million in the third quarter. Bob Swan, eBay's CRO, noted during an earnings call, however, that the company sold $485 million of equity in flash sale site RueLaLa and ShopRunner to partially finance the that deal. eBay's Marketplaces recorded $2 billion in revenues, up 12% year over year, while its Enterprise division experienced a meager 5% increase to $238 million in the third quarter, offset by a reduced take rate. Swan noted that marketing services were impacted by eBay's recent efforts to consolidate nine business units within the enterprise division. Mobile was a keyword for the quarter, with eBay CEO John Donahoe calling it "transformative" for commerce. PayPal has 137 million active accounts globally and this quarter brought "significant updates" to the mobile app. Donahoe said he expects the Braintree acquisition to "significantly accelerate" PayPal's scope in Q4.

Facebook Site Retargeting

 

Facebook is launching another retargeting tool, separate from FBX, that will allow a website owner to serve ads on mobile and desktop via custom audiences. It's like the Facebook version of Google AdWords site retargeting, but it's called Website Custom Audiences. FB's new retargeting will also work separately from established retargeting platforms such as Turn and Triggit -- it's self-serve and lacks the bells and whistles of dynamic creative, for example. Read the blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03Blz7Pq2oHb5a1Li0bLV8QJy7yjNN9QPlhnX23oZtVqIs8WK9I5ovOPl_yiDJfRfASm8NwEhI-3SXckrWC8wpYOqakNpks4rJabrrzgEPSPHLjESl-P5qJFTJxassDAXtp2RMxPZkN5-IatKIibekp-ye9PJRZ0ocf8ju-R-Fq_1A==>  Facebook product marketing manager Scott Shapiro discusses the different flavors of retargeting with Ad Age (FBX/Custom Audiences): "A travel client will use FBX to retarget people who've gone searching for hotels and then show them that exact hotel [they saw]. ... They'll use custom audiences to reach people who are searching for hotels but have not downloaded their mobile app on iOS 7 on iPad." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03A30JzuRgnM9-RT4trrYnO4EXByyr5lYn6ZdZ0BlTwMQeozPc7aDOos_4twxTe0ofm1cD4CKPAdhgM7OivoXHOqGIP_lC_vKjFlE6uW_81mNHulGPEIUuEz967PBcGfCu56iWjVigjVVZv2H71lZENEr90AWcv-DeUlw0B1jlsfrWjFKeI_XdwlWVmz5zgp208EphFClC2CdA==> .

 

Katz Back

 

Former interclick (acquired by Yahoo in 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03AfSifmSOm8rZ8qbt-2Z55S_XkOtGe4RMrz_TOK8JhbkjKHPnixz0-Nh5sLQo3iVw7za-okxjt4uQotl51GoPfu1ed16kIMtTc-b2ryoZXHzJnOZnLurp0bLcMwhMR-2xvhyHH2chMf5ANyc9IXXifuEqV6QtswpMwbv4XX_5lqyw==> ) CEO Michael Katz is "back" as the CEO and co-Founder of mobile data platform company mParticle <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03Cvb2sHbFBU0B1_fLVFxZV7x64yuu1LoRXO_bzfsSfnM-DfoY39TIzAT44IXfvtSDQOvrvdV-CxoOfal_XcKHI_I4YnHi_wQmG5yRjr-NE9rQ==>  which announced the closing a $3 million round of seed funding yesterday. In addition to Katz, the company includes many of the same core group from interclick. "Ultimately, we're making mobile data activation seamless, and enabling app owners to spend more time creating the best possible consumer experience by providing them with a proper data framework," said Katz in a statement. The round was led by Mike Brown Jr <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03Ch9e0JCy62xYDTYaAl0VHXYo8ujA8NHrTYg1VY2TxeV0kEV1OOfjoHeKyzGFFZSCkYM2RCJkVfzvNEJMpv0bbdWvlR7e5lBaS-gj15a7SbL27VpLgtoNRZI7fxRuEX9PUbe63BiVg1QmpUkTq7Q--wg2dvwMKA7uwlyTND2ELG-iOV9bC6B_b2> .'s Bowery Capital along with Google Ventures, Greylock Partners and several angel investors. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03DMuJ4AqIS9Wjf19_ZtnZR7O-Wtepr1jMzDBJtg3EsBcFsGkQwbNnuN3gHvXyGfR-R04e1oahqYcRfoIJdITvmv1N_cj4gAmm6LlgNL1HJkqVQASu6k3fFGLF7ZdNIbvD6ENaa8nKOv_9W3SOerOEyqyToR27e-QhZ2IRg_zjO5wCcJzVGSPT5hMGP_FOkGzl27cUR67IgthQEkuldl3OCI8_2fhzHqyFF2ELyLXrJZdLKi-mrrrTr3akyyXsR8w8XJ0t4CaazlpSvR5AFdLOspqaQHKi1D_wtNi5mkJZ9M0g==> .

 

About Ad Network 2.0

 

BMO Capital Markets' Dan Salmon offered his thoughts on ad-buying platform Rocket Fuel's future in a note to investors this week. Investment thesis: "We believe the company's growing exposure to nondisplay inventory (i.e., online video, social and mobile) is vital to maintaining hypergrowth; international opportunities seem to be underestimated by investors at the moment. The company's strong technology requires consistent innovation to maintain its lead, but the company also differentiates itself with a strong sales and services organization. Long term, investors remain focused on the sustainability of gross margins, and we expect pressure over the long term. But the transition to nondisplay revenue is helping sustain and grow them in the near term, and the potential to evolve into more of a platform model (as Rocket Fuel has with its Japanese affiliate) could help address some of these concerns." Rocket Fuel is valued at just over $2 billion.

 

Ad Server Of The Future

 

On his personal blog, kbs+'s Darren Herman thinks hard about the ad servers to come. He reasons, "As the media agency model adopts owned/earned (they traditionally handle 'paid'), the need for serving and tracking content emerges. The format of choice for traditional ad servers [is] banners but this will change and we see ad servers serving almost any sized unit. From this paragraph forward in the post, I use the [words] Content Servers as the new ad server." Read the proceeding paragraphs <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03BYrww4rZfUbyyyC1fv08pBPa73N9VtJs8WDkdDSfXJIFCvfnIiWh1MBH9TU8JKLE_KoCcYXmrDvVyWpubbqbftkN1OVc2xw6iGUlOcmYbuhBvWhd5_GYzhLM5ed3gRhp8g6swpJFM0B1Ua5_7aYjxBA6OmsChRkc61lbPOF5lerpv2Pce0P8jrgBNpWTFe7bE=> .

 

When I Was A Client

 

In a feature in Adweek, new CMO Erin Matts of Omnicom's Annalect compares her experience in the agency to when she was on the client side (Anheuser-Busch InBev): "The things I thought as an agency person were important don't even affect me as a client. As a client, advertising isn't about solving ad problems. It's a byproduct of your business problem. On new business pitches, as soon as I walked in the door, I'd be thinking, what story is going to play well in that room. As a client, it was, I've heard that story before." Read the full interview here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xO_OCGIX03D_vP9w2qed_nKo4Tx6sPUCiQ2pCqH_YuD8UX3I464ub1x8qg9-yqTKXaP4edU_pqE-tBQjG-XRbG99KdqT2aRyeESOKiF9oCe-jauYVidOQjneFX30-BOnDaw7uZCWB_Q0crGGJ7e058SkS2X_5th5nGxgUZuHdw3vuQq55grz9BfX8q7F31rVDCq6ludHTX1YtetHaeH0G1fCNIZe8-qBGE_77QWFS7J9OFS8icRl0Q==> .

The problem of fraud could be even worse than people realize, according to a new report from Adweek's Mike Shields. Along with the usual suspects, there are sites like Crackle and CollegeHumor that may employ robotic means in order to drive traffic, in spite of their well-known brands. Furthermore, companies like Facebook, AOL and Yahoo, which pride themselves on being premium publishers, could also be vulnerable to fraudulent traffic. Most exposed companies claim to be working on solutions, but some of the worst offenders just go on to create new sites and start the process over again. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elWr95dEd4wtxUuB8lVlEmYy3_CsGz1CUDKYhZrHn7fZ1E0U8om770il1brO2I4djsP6PkxuSU33T3zwZfm2PTNDfmU0iKJt6ODTswvz8OrTbu-LoNRMa3OvAl8I6xGZJpABpFj7aPgGKuKj72lh-1ZbsEdFRVi8vJpTQj2aVQCH3UFrUoqYUBkcNvaf1zCV5H8NTUARqcO5BHQbsgAolKVWHxTkGlfaP9Bf_CVOMjqLXg==> .

 

Compression Acquisition

 

Facebook has made an acquisition of a mobile startup from Israel called Onavo <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elWKfkQiE_TN8_AMpKKIy-PEHhzhmZfKQJ8p-6RrvB1nahSwA8EJ_llhvyGZk1f03DUtzFIze6rTAFIEhoooV7SD26-r5pL8FQY3Ix5AtYtKLg==>  that focuses on data compression. ''We expect Onavo's data compression technology to play a central role in our mission to connect more people to the Internet, and their analytic tools will help us provide better, more efficient mobile products,'' a Facebook spokesman told T <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elXqYkNeshkLk8aELcNB4nmwJ4AkgtppJdwD5OW-HVWS-2gHl7Pjccwvi1a9y8EDHQwIfltPWn94h_JrF7fgc1K6lYU11D6a3Y00FCfi2ONj6_mCLs7uXfPfJu4szorfCgYRAKNvDslnGODvXiQ9Fo1UXghXojHC_QjPwt6CA1Gv2vi6QtD9VltYaUEnePCLq757DbAiYJk4rVPusTY5v3BqyxMmuDeCfKw=> he New York Times <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elVQC-YkmIGJUF2Bbq4Wmph6cVaZ6yyl-bWaYfZy5P8MYYCs-GRJWHN7DduVEVw6WWQqxh5Ay3oG909gNfkjpE7GXp6I_YZWH0raaKZbEi-M7XWDRgjmueuHGSMeYgiIyHwfxPVRUISfTNkEbZU7KkiQJezeRkExA1fPz1CL0_rmb08I5OTi68CNLGoiJy0ewFy1hd1oR711jXAje5NBYUO-zSV9S_gG8XI=> . As noted in the official press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elUNpWUStaCZ6rbM7LL_wM-xzVJcIZesYQm8fm3VeGWRefhWsL9Tek2C6r4qkiWI-2Lp55pOCIylJNqBx4VNROV8-4Ih0G-nTY5TbeqOCHBcwmb8X3hhmDtfiZ8gfLNOfnpKnlbPGq3EM6HFY2tOKt8P>  from Onavo, this acquisition also will help Facebook in its Internet.org initiative to make the Internet more accessible to people around the world. TechCrunch points out that this acquisition could help entice developers much like its purchase of Parse <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elVcdKKb02_7EcI0CMjTTygLY3z86TtZd5ruLOvVWO94OL92Up4xF9JbQSz1zhC_2FRcfI7yBRjbJScxZGiF69Kcagwf3o8F4YAy5e_ZktHbb8cqhR04zb70ueq7oa9E7Au3WGwfMLm9zL9GW5iwXO1c2mS2KZBpjbgy-Wm9jyTuUPlO4X_oZZ7qZCVlgT5rvfcnpsN9Bb6nVw==>  did. Read the story here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elUU-3BWLe_MQQBCC80sd-SDghnhUB2rTxqhNih51nEkkMugwuW1Mw2PLE6546ttNG-g8Z3UVAyyXZo49wzADGZlS6nhyEM9wwQrnaa31krKBZyC6tBToXRzaT_cKyXC3JV3PWI6t50WVNfHnktZ0JJ71_CVoycFZ1EwMRI2x3yfprUIogTcDAFQal1r-0hSOdF5H-OxjXNJSoMM8yq3mf6NXqlUURSAJkL_2fJqBXqhRD5eL0m8qhkH> .

 

What Should Twitter Do

 

Twitter's MoPub acquisition may give it the edge it needs to attract more advertiser dollars as its IPO nears and help Twitter build a broader ad exchange, says the Financial Times. Unlike Facebook, Twitter would allow advertisers to use its data on other sites, rather than just its own. "Advertisers are frustrated that they can't reach audiences more effectively on their mobile device. Any innovation that makes it easier for advertisers to do that accurately with high-quality data, targeting and measurement has a high chance of being successful," said Xaxis CEO Brian Lesser. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elV9pnQhFFWwGfL1Y4iVypazkyOqoyNIjy6p7e0wRm5_zSzjLgKY0QGZpch-sgU0nZwz_xSD5alo5DDm2aOX5bSOOdPNWxVU53BMeixH1c0_UEpIeOv0T-dTgBRP_N9grk0Bdnoz3NxkQ9Y0-eMW3DAopwWwOx3lXzAECmL6fSt1vlozblFSqr0qw97aod1ma2Ube6_imJQiYA==> .

 

Agencies Vs. Ad Tech

 

Agencies and ad tech are increasingly at odds as vendors and marketers realize they don't necessarily need the agencies, according to Ad Age. "What we thought was valuable and proprietary [in the agency] -- the algorithms and bidder -- is the most commoditized part [of the business]," said Quentin George, co-founder and principal of Unbound. "The application of data and understanding audiences is where real value is." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elVwBfl4FbDeaDIxfiGf9Ic24h8-V_AhJTdqR0WX0llqamEL7SPaGPZJ6SJ5zxURcb_MCIbHMJ27sGiF89U-XDBp0MnoSZUFSYwPn5amMLi8TRJMzZN6UyEYTyK7Vs31OmUYyDRotcH5_qXGsqeSXWc0B7fXio-JHqlrYxkWqaUOjehhTO6U_fho9LKbJxsPweQhBvP5TV3CYQ==> . Marco Bertozzi, executive managing director of VivaKi EMEA, disagrees with this sentiment and believes the cost of figuring out RTB and then maximizing its benefits is too much for a lot of companies. He created a long list of steps it takes to fully implement RTB and writes, "Advertisers may well do this themselves, and some do, but what I have seen so far are advertisers who say they do it themselves but really then lean on third parties, no different to using a trade desk." Read his blog post here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elWMKa2BhAM-yD87nr3K7FjYLFGQ6gbnQ0O-zpuxqAKOqeh5Ive9vMRd8ZjffftnDbVhaSVI1j7inf_RiVP_AxONZ7pdF-b4ML4hNx_ehaN0TGu4GuEU_Pi2d18MkjWpbzhBqqAGj_tgOzmRmQB80bhMpTT0jRs1-pgx20JAdZZaJvUtnQ_U6v0WteETWCTN6jU=> .

 

Catching Up With Michael Barrett

 

Peter Kafka of AllThingsD picks former AdMeld CEO Michael Barrett's brain in a Q&A about the current state of display advertising. Some of the highlights include Barrett's belief that Facebook's data won't necessarily beat third-party data. Furthermore, a cookieless future would have a negative impact on advertising. "If you look at the rates people are monetizing mobile right now. ... Most publishers, if they suddenly had rates plummet on the display side, it would be crushing," he said. Read the interview here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elVKh4oMutGN3L_IAbEqz5b1q_qgTwwCuDX5Cdaz-r1nIh1WInCGRfYrR8kq_ZyhoohEzMzDVrdf5Pubd_zyedkgSUrOpMYZuXGh03AlTBU0iP5qph-m6ahITkf8URlmXcRtBRIKhGqt0RzkKUUk5YmNwyTJXYNKxPjRgNyG5qngUautnMC3HSgenl3G2CeHdzRnEM9K7HSXhA8Qd7GNDYYyundFX9_Fzl0=> .

Cookie Match

 

Inside Facebook's Dennis Yu gets to look at a marketer's match rates for Facebook's Custom Audience product and finds a big difference between B2B email lists (20%) and B2C (up to 80%). A "match" is made when an email address for a user of an ecommerce site is matched to a cookie on Facebook using a user's Facebook login email. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mcKYeJ17elUm02A0sAkrJeTPNu9xBfRP0w5CfHexvguqSzt658tHBgY14Vbnq1m8JNkvpVDKiZAL62lz7JkNcvWb68zmMG9lOs0Zv9laDIX2Y3hMp185pOzrj0SjTnvWS_Co1uulXnHP5QpHJq_lBlbTMoqd0PXmpVOMSg9MVLbqeegUUwYuITUw0WYuoU7TlxRzbKZJ8UbHX8xK0QmGnQ==> .

 

Solving For The Times

 

New York Times CEO Mark Thompson tells a reporter from his own paper that driving yield using an array of offerings is inevitable for the company. The Times' Christine Haughney writes, "The plans vary from news-based products, like video, mobile apps and expanded international coverage, to tangential revenue producers like one-day conferences and cruises featuring Times reporters and columnists as expert speakers." Recommended Ad

 

Google may be inserting a Google+ recommendation of yours -- called "Shared Endorsements" -- into an ad, according to changes announced by the company on Friday. Google's terms-of-service page provides a use case: "For example, your friends might see that you rated an album 4 stars on the band's Google Play page. And the +1 you gave your favorite local bakery could be included in an ad that the bakery runs through Google. We call these recommendations shared endorsements and you can learn more about them here." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku227wrD1_npc1DmHPdN2mghD7MP7OVd1iPCYgluhXr7ols0zG69f9QrV6uT82IO7kINmOMW8b8K0lk6SaebwxEIkyb7oLMR5M3fvRQ8Fo6k3lvG9fxy6OM41cp6MA5O_Z8wjuZiPoXhvgLhbYpH86pfw>  Bryan Wiener, CEO of 360i, tells the WSJ (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku215zjJqq6-eBGAU4reKXNsh_PCq-zDdRxRQjPEVZOt_sf-2Yb_i9CAbRxDsxNqhyLMJidZDyz-HeW1q6OfuZeaOlbxoBawbYnO-yRcycWpy5goK-OcEsWTODF-MSDa1oUuexnJF-NrGm4dVqXVJS6oKmZCe5NMwBlKYJP4hU_lsxXRJjSipraRh>  that "clicking +1s isn't yet an ingrained consumer behavior in the vein of clicking on a Facebook 'like.'" The New York Times notes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku20bDz2FTD5GrRqdz_KLFwVdFalnOSi_4WkQlCj0WvoenOT0l_oM01PvpwVtP8sfBIUH9e3H1Z_NdxlIGNmOrOVRTYmHWqp5X_X5qSl1lccD2QcknSgv87Dsj-CdWGwdhbrSkYFy5-AsiiXXGyT7jbIuIhJYf9GzbOZUzlGq6IP9o4w4ZOajnXs4EqOiRwKbNRjv9DkghWeoz7PJBGI5BRBR>  that this echoes Facebook's inclusion of recommendations in ads, including its own search results.

 

Acqui-Hire In Sunnyvale

 

Yahoo has acquired Bread -- a social ads-personalization company -- according to CEO Alan Chan on his company's site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku230MMn_tYbFja30vpNnPeja5Jy5OHmbE97TzgNMjphQOHWUF35dCVi7GzAXnFo4fEUURuQ9QXsofuctcP5RPlP-Jmp7bqvK6Eg=> , "We are thrilled to join Yahoo's advertising team in Sunnyvale, where we will be working on developing next-generation solutions for social and mobile publishers and advertisers." Seven Bread employees will join the company, says TechCrunch's John Constine, who ponders aloud, "Marissa Mayer has been focused on buying consumer startups as of late, but Bread's team could strengthen the ad products that monetize Yahoo's properties. Together they might be able to turn all of the Yahoo feel-good momentum into real revenue." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku22fNqmtfF4BzkuABjBmDfBMLwT_JRgHKchntjSccjmfVIxqdqW4FDZQk0CTuN1PY_fgQmngcD26zKNlapC34qR5a_OxFdFYCOF4I7lvo0_DbmXaE24cDpA3oeZ_dR5Dj0jcxDXrEpTxLSasOT_oRBvKATSlTniUyAU=> 

 

Scrutiny Club

 

Every form of targeting has seen its share of scrutiny from Washington, and now cross-device ad targeting will be joining the club. With the end of the third-party cookie growing nearer, advertisers are turning to fingerprinting, as Ad Age points out. "Such tracking envelopes [sic] users in a digital environment where marketers know their preferences and personal information no matter which device they use while consumers are kept largely in the dark," wrote Ed Markey in a letter. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku21hro5ovSugm1NbMSg-cAPNnQzhgEptIynXKuGoW2IITpJz_Gf7E6neZZdQW_yFVh0s7OUJQrh7pPAMklRCpAJvlfTQ305agoafOrA9amp4QhtVk14OgRD0GWhIW_usH-5UgUUdFcrl4x4Cfqml1ySQkVh2_t_BMUwbIDTA20RDl4ZkWeG1TokroYq3Rb9kc5Y2GIQFaa0b4oh3m1TmhlnJ> .

 

Native Network

 

Mobile ad network Airpush has made an acquisition of mobile native advertising Hubbl. "Hubbl's approach to mobile advertising moves beyond traditional mobile ads to create personalized in-app content experiences for users," said Kushal M. Choksi, founder and CEO of Hubbl. "This creates a win-win scenario where users get a better experience while developers earn significantly higher revenue." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku207eIul_OJyW5dB1IxmHNYmkbE0-XRn1A1kMT9rJA5n1jft0RMcqSPvpL_dCH3ZmezookDRa5U9eU6vPd1JX792kqJs0DadZLcdhgDsj75UXKUfis0eI_3rX-YphFwOoWrn71JaL2s2pNWt4Uoupo0ko9o5HCWCTFSJOVbxqj750wdE4CinRk5lEYfLnlse93c=> .

 

Addressing Home Improvement

 

Lowe's is wielding the power of mobile technology in stores to bring online and offline data together in hopes of achieving the holy grail of one-to-one, addressable communication. In an eMarketer interview with Sean Bartlett, Lowe's director of mobile strategy and platforms, he outlined how purchase history can be tied to a customer's key fob, eliminating the need for receipts. Store associates also carry iPhones that give them customer information as well as inventory. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku23vsWEFIvxxjgrLiL5y2j2Xs5wyJ0JK4lMLfwYjkf2YCB1G9Y1vlLAuWigOM_YllpXP7YcEx00HX_HLdM0LF2uSeYuH0XrU6PxyFBFu7nlqCMHSt_AvSbouagnQq_tQQst9LKFxoERjIPAW55ScAqQZu6ct5w-jxizs0Bw6P-zAibOX7podaeBLqKeolmjJq_Cs-I5faO6N4DGpcXlEzu7M> .

Fraud Impression

 

Vertical ad network Gourmet Ads has been stepping up its tech efforts against fraud, according to a blog post by founder Benjamin Christie. He writes, "The technology now measures every single impression served both across our directly managed network of food sites and when we buy impressions in the AppNexus Exchange. The main goal of this monitoring was to ensure our client's advertising was being viewed by real humans and not computerized bots." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010q_gQaPku20diE37UWtJXQao2kpglny3kbrU-9Dlbb3SsWDYlfzI8oCmEAhWodRZLNowoKt1D8z3xTEP37JcSKfmYFCEIqVzRmXymVgxBYBbDVF0H0F5AvppZfAgDesNdhTigTd_AR2AUpA9GVGFM-JGKDrEntbV> .
