Twitter Slip

 

Twitter accidentally spilled the date of its IPO, PrivCo has uncovered. In a financial document, Twitter pegged Feb. 15, 2014, as the end of the lock-up agreement -- typically 90 days after an IPO. Hence the offering will be Nov. 15. PrivCo CEO Sam Hamadeh told VentureBeat the slip is "emblematic of how rushed Twitter's IPO planning is." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YPJzqwWNSftpyDIkRhr-rtsdED-uNiZm24jSPR-WHc6i5xO9VsxZVc1AhXF0seicEB_ZxUUHOkTrwfnXVCMft3-zvo2cg25gUxPaBlKoMKWQ5-WL8Y2Jfj_6PdKIaaWzu1k3ec2gMNCtLJmR6yTgD0HZ_XaF4V0hRtuTsWuzrPzzYro24OzNiX6aATBj2foB5AjcBkAW0sCSg==> .

 

Cookie Savior

 

From his Upstream Group blog, Doug Weaver delivers a faux encomium on Google's reported initiatives to kill the third-party cookie with its own solution -- known among the cognoscenti as AdID <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YMldGEGcQa8fH3At5CR1s9hFhlj_rgBcOkLCieuuwfVPXvC6TYDUFEx02alxh-R4DGblGHqqRmsfcESoVhAHI1mkBoLhIJS5oreO5_x90oCfP9kHEcEuG6BKf2qfSV11zFu9uGl81mDn6zXi1yj-NaAYDbW2hCfrV0DE8_qLa1204HqGdKSdZgZ0xDlCIY9iX2wjO93D8wt9g==> . Weaver shoots from his digital quill, "I think I speak for the entire industry and for all current and future Web users when I say, 'Thank God! We needs us some more Google!'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YMxtZkjr3AMp9tmck2j44I30TevRWH4VsobeZk_Vyt-2I05QfCGSF_2h8UuOnv7hhV_5-VUOP_8xufWVD9qAQm_Co8UN3w-yI28SmOeZr5ONYSJsJQhSpKR6DbvrOw5MHwcpYmR7jlbIA==> 

 

Opera Mediaworks

 

Mobile ad platform Opera Mediaworks is seeing large gains and shared several stats today highlighting the company's growth. A spin-off of Opera Software, Opera Mediaworks' revenue grew 106% between Q2 2012 and this year, and the company is projecting its revenue for 2013 will be more than $100 million. More than 13,000 sites and apps use the San Mateo, Calif.-based company's platform and it serves 60 billion ad impressions a month, reaching 400 million global consumers. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YOZRU7ElYT98HBI7B4DJVggPx27eoayaNr3hmGK-llK7v1wjAG85uuzCXE8hmb9d25U8lQSd1dRb65gDCOHsUhama7l0PoH1gvF1pNv5PpkAB8L2pfHegXQcnW8-nWpLy4-xOuaW6oJygeNWh_HTm3DKsSi9eCJ6Jo=> 

 

Better Conversion Through Design

 

Retailers focused on app design are finding better conversion rates, according to Mobile Commerce Daily. Both Sears and Gilt have found that an emphasis on a personalized experience and more streamlined checkout have increased sales through mobile. "Our suggestions are to make the mobile experience so quick and easy they don't take the time to check, and to make up for price with customer service, shipping guarantees and discounts, and other promotional opportunities," said Paige Mazzoni, VP of marketing at MarketLive. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YPgivPba5j5ighSqKgZweFzYWE2pqbVpYs_EJyAA267zh4CgB_3wC3VFHMGaQiCGoX7L3Pv0oU0BUhZe6_WxNxqQ0j4JN-vR1G2eL87ycDBlyVk2S0o4t6yqf_UVEfqt7YF6FJxn2IUm0y9uHdQKGphlIMGCf3Kj3hiIoKTV_d_LZnCvHzG4qEXzpm9zGINkXZIHqjFwmicEOf0260y6YUwHjCDCI_mM5k=> .

 

LiquidM Launch

 

San Francisco-based startup LiquidM unveiled a platform to help ad networks, trading desks and other mobile media buyers manage their mobile ad campaigns. The company also raised a $5 million Series A from Blumberg Capital, Earlybird Venture Capital and Asset Management Ventures. "Most mobile campaigns are managed through a mix of in-house technology and point solutions, some of which weren't specifically built for mobile," CEO Christof Wittig told AdExchanger. "What makes us different is that we're offering a full-stack platform that allows you to manage your premium and performance ads." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YN7nWvT1_f0-dQqSI06xDjffk0sSOx8AGln0oPFHe8pzTZxNdqUvWLcGWNxeI_bg8TEOpMmbiPlw1wmzawtwYgvJuEunHIDlvss-UD4uTjmKc_BA5hyALwbqaC0b1YK_HuoPIMweF6RYGh_6iDigoyhs1uo1wseD8KQOXuT08Iju_siUzVZtfORZQO-OrqFSmmoShh4ZR8Z8LaaBGXvs2Vy9uC6pDrDQn9gWGevztOwz6ZfePNAsEfve55NTXMTCUL-r891BpNJUK5OLTbySSAez9Aic25Zt_mpENyD4NIlMY_mTnQWxO2GNssNz3AVXhE=>

I'm Not Dead Yet

 

The pageview metric is supposed to be dead by now, but it isn't, Brian Abelson points out in a blog post. And the doomsayers, some of whom offer their own alternatives, aren't helping things. "Instead of worrying about whether we're measuring the wrong things, or using the wrong tools or software, or falling behind the competition, let's take a deep breath, ignore the doomsayers and do the best we can with what we have right now. And, if after a while, that's still not working, then perhaps we should reassess precisely why, in what manner and by whom we were convinced that analytics would solve our problems in the first place." Read the post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001R5TSKGoD2YPfLgj-Mb9hpl_PvM1Xh-XpgCnIUXpD1iwQi_8sN55qIoNlLCY0AwSBh9OmUqd_hGS88LTT8tUFGhKgmhapBjoq_apwsFVGbdv46MHKWv68l3yi0ItVNo4p-5o-tFmFHArmGS0AFJBXB7c7p0i1o-stzQ-6ihzZbOEd9ffXDmfPE_XcyJMryLun3X7mY0XxwD4=> .

Do Not Track, We Will

 

Microsoft was the first browser maker to turn on "Do Not Track" by default, and now its advertising arm plans to implement a proprietary tracking system. Microsoft would track across computers, phones and tablets that are running Windows, as well as Xbox consoles, Internet Explorer and Bing, an unnamed source told Ad Age's Tim Peterson. "Not only would [Microsoft] be building out an Ad ID, but they would also be building out a cross-channel attribution model, which everybody wants," said The Media Kitchen President Barry Lowenthal. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVwsuwRG9x5DfuLfzBnaCcsCYQTOAHX4cZ6gAXQmXpPVz6GuyFWjPnzDY1j5ViNItsC00Dof9wcj3TqlmXWZ0MKUNMUaDwp5lAaqvF-mEBtdeEvLgA6d-1wWGYgyqBzwur6i8tC01zJ_ioX9ZQbJtnByT98Y05jg26hfem1WjmhVB5S8wq1lbzmXot2SrRZB4enbMUWfwqckg6lbY5qDPLRz> .

 

Bigger Isn't Better

 

Big data and good data are not the same thing, according to Dana Hayes Jr., GVP, global partner development at Acxiom. In a column for ClickZ, Hayes Jr. says siloed databases are a logjam to targeting nirvana. The way out? "Predicting people's intentions, or propensity modeling, is what takes you from a blind distraction with big data and into smart, better data implementation for targeted reach." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVy1S9Egrw3HqVh9EFKHDEdkJkPFlGbSoWQryrJKR870fCFcTk6o6Mqqxv1S-RWePHBcKlzuv0QIb9vq-ymAfhHdq3mhs92hOoLnW92bAOwzRirUL9AyM973SlaO0i-9tHLkDpsZrP9JLoJJqEhYbUucxtJO597h11-JDBo4toiHr_txHwkUXMGZeU5dQbWWSjVstCRtQg0xY0EQ3PWiYSoiReDFnW2qZtU=> .

 

Unloyal

 

Companies love their loyalty programs, but only 35% of members redeem rewards, according to Direct Marketing News, and a Forrester report. "There's a shift in focus from the idea that loyalty is all about transactions and discounts. In the future it needs to be more about engagement and emotion," said Forrester analyst Emily Collins. Forrester recommends embracing two-way interaction, balancing rewards and experiences and bridging the strategy and technology gap. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVy-j-qgL4UdeUshJuitSsvd2nMDGOicBjmHzm4DDN3ft6C7_b29hJY3hxbH1yCsousddeJxBPNqB3_QbCCJgnRMbsMUtC-jV2E8Pbe7bbLvOwiMNXru9w3ydoQwrVSNi2g16XONyBkPpXDu2ytYQagLwyfCaCnpsSOLZbxx9d5mpLFjdbiHm42is_avh0Iv3p4=> .

 

Pin-closure

 

Pinterest has begun testing a "Promoted Pins" paid media program first announced in September. A label indicates a pin is promoted, and a mouse-over gives the user more information. "We encourage brands to have an authentic presence on Pinterest that shows what makes their brand unique, and give people inspiration to take action offline with those pins," a spokeswoman said to AllThingsD in an email. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVzXfE4GQC-qJ1LoBxyCgOJrj6zOZoOou8Xvysin_3zYpxnkvnqWZfPtz0V6oEokzO0FJ9-I23PedH3b_9TOY_OisWtpoJ_sw_j5sW5vTlaPPsALNO3785g6oqyWie3XCAemW7pK-EsJw6pO1PGzyQvfwO9whmmCK_mPwNYI5Ku-eQ==> .

 

India Ecommerce

 

Amazon may be the ecommerce winner in the U.S., but Flipkart takes the cake in India. A new $160 million round brings its total capital raised to $540 million, according to VentureBeat. The company competes heavily with Amazon in India, with both trying to cash in on the growing middle class that increasingly prefers the convenience of shopping online. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVwLaL9HD8tf2nwK9JDIhyXkXdmTArFtkCf7eFJcajX1ZhXe4IN_8ReDPZaVzUVpXqvipr5c-lviRWR7d663X1UpzEnjY8eND9XbEZvd1yHaQfsFVnDN45kWh-C2dlB6PXm-xSg6jgbhAvenCAGAZy5AwGFYC5KEDrsset_zQpWvqT1duzLyioJ9eaY4iLxm_szgn8FtWnH_zAVpHT9cHMxD> .

Leveraging Survey Data

 

SessionM is finding success with its loyalty and rewards platform and is launching its Mobile Custom Audience Segmentation Tool, or mCAST. SessionM allows users to earn rewards for interacting with apps in certain ways, and now the company will bring that data along with other first-party data to its platform. "What we've found is that when you give consumers control, transparency and tangible value, they are more than willing to reciprocate by giving you their attention and valuable insights into who they are and what they like," said Bill Clifford, chief revenue officer for SessionM. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVzwTpbokZ9r9UvAh8E0fmviH4hvV8_iIiklbWtWl-DtllZWjyxDDL72AsZgbewp9kAenkywQlx1gvi0nnqKdl_rVf7JDIRFHav56HISbvFJPYqwGi1HWsuwcf03Lv_pkRpY-DAz9C1xf-GpkaGH3ACgLoC-xM7D9g6LLeNXGD-0YkH_QY6zQynFs7dS6eQbqN-Mih5YCNoSoUAZpeBF2nIRCsmOBM5PaBc=> .

 

More Facebook Updates

 

Facebook is on an update roll, this time refreshing its Page Insights tool to give page owners a better idea of who is engaged with their post, and who isn't. Facebook simplified the metrics used and updated the export tool. The company also made it clear that there are no plans the make the "people talking about this" metric public. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVzPqgaGMOI9mJUT_LbD3VwkEPJOu9wU02BSWY8WkzLOkIjFD3DXLwwl63RY_mz3CwC4gwc5owZxSxY-1MhXp1lZNlIWqLX6BPtwKkgVGDJc4og2efYSr1DX-yZo44rMQSjrql1lBa7U8GkL__K0KdCkrA--xrumVP0zExyI189y1w==> .

 

Mo' Screens

 

Americans are spending less time in front of the TV, but not much, while adding in content from other devices, according to eMarketer. This leaves the average person at more than five hours in front of a computer (or phone, or tablet) and four-and-a-half hours in front of the TV. In a self-experiment, WSJ's Katherine Rosman Rosman found is that it's actually difficult to log the amount of time she spent consuming content. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001q0-KligHWVw5LIEkq6TwFU5AYVeRF6c4P4k4Z4_4ERACvF3S6Smhi5II9n-nZMTbi7y594iEwktjUdpMgE6rfVO6wHxqSBYBaEXcKvwRA8UlpCl6APfi1R6FQ2DH_WF8hLxyj8tg-sFHRjrxT-dcQ_PQj0Q6qUIGfh1qbmo7LQxvlZ-TD5Ml0QsbKhcrfTcS> .

DG Loves Rich Media

 

TechCrunch's Anthony Ha reports that DG has made what appears to be an acqui-hire of sorts with its purchase of 11-person rich media vendor Republic Project <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyiUhuKg-Hta6Fwe2rMh99XRjSu9vl7NU7C_UqncA9enIwcZ2XcOrIibVxGhNj17tuzahJ_rwsJBoxDY2X7rjkzN-jwxvwVdBoybK6qNwsi730bf-FeFzJYK>  for a reported $1.4 million plus earn-outs. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyjYVmjF3Hgn8TcT9MXwuavi9rzZUikdiF_ZJ2wq9uIRoa_VObv-tmaRPn7N6fzszHoqjVH4yF646A0J8m2pCqQN_EBs4U9VFa0QLnaWBYE4spwCfrvyNbT3HkGfcgViMP50GhVASKjLK_7u0KDhJn84j6KSRkWO-VIh9XPtoq29uA==> . Republic pitches a cross-device integration capability with its cloud-based offering. Prior to selling its TV ad distribution business to Extreme Reach this summer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyhTLI_vQtAQhugMtZxGQJUmf4Kbtmuo2gFalP_ugxq5-BRzf3DEGC5pium8fmfv_0Lmu0REjm6-DO7DUFXOCZ5WQQxDVQRJZdVGxtt3V7Dy0eETaUlRoqwuSdqNewAIpGPXwvgfATQnkDQDAJbKvC7FxvMl1RTJzxk8517YWBmQLHNXXRS4jPsOEvPoBmGCQh-jmqGdmVDuJ_CcGFpNVfz3ZpLYVZUOhkU=> , DG has a history of purchasing rich media vendors - such as MediaMind <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyhlwC54U7pKP0XtYCjJ6p1tyHMx4F1e93wfscnZ9y5cjmYPKfPXqHdpH5rfR-M5I1ax04lqrY0ZAtiGnHlxZs2XsCPd7shiyi6ZQrxeckicburAkt_yr4XwwC8AabBn3Xm_y7pWOzR0J69Mvuf2xFIZAOVQ_FnRb50Di-ENTItUpcxZUdU-yEWCdymmeUpM0KulFOL-pda7EQ==>  (which was Eyeblaster), Eyewonder <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyijLosA7c1KdgapgIZJ1ZBsM86rKTp65NLhPeAOuP7LKwlviIXn7ndK6tZ9t87xKogZfJT5FaniAGlx7OrydOh8I36iaATqpy5ZeSR6UPl474cFqr4ruKUae3WylDXk4sE21nYbcdhBiMswk4pzkJgdVAU2KdIeRZoa5k5F4NCnFQ==>  and Unicast. It also purchased semantic tech company Peer39 in 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyicu6LXesdfum7JqW9sNiZPZ0Vi_gVtOGZZjyqBIBTDCLbz7tnnRKtvS3sD3FGpltvfaXpNGLRNOosq9B7JLQhru6xUOyRaV6mnLBG20jXsbVrQblul9v2nGEpo0T7lYtPop0Rz9jIKlCC2Hvw-2KrVbdc3zBA7yfg=> .

 

Ad Shifting

 

The New York Times reviewed what DVR and on-demand technology is doing to the television industry and found that a lot of networks are experiencing huge jumps in viewer numbers - in some cases seven days after a show premieres. The problem is convincing advertisers to still pay for their time slots knowing that a lot of people fast forward through commercials on recorded TV. Networks like Fox are trying to push viewers to use video on demand rather than DVR because they are able to block fast forwarding that way. "Most viewing is still occurring during the first three days, but if more viewing continues to shift to four-to-seven, or beyond, we won't be getting fully compensated," Joe Earley, COO of Fox Broadcasting, said in an email. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyjDpNtzqIRKwEJM3zh54NOOiga2_4pCYBtBYtbVHb6ac2xHIrSs_3luLxxHuwsrePHULFDbEl3xoFNaQGP20hlCQ4rw6LzV11Y0IaZByVc2aoSKkC1p2MieO6Kl0WZih3Jk9qjfdyV9ZuqlfWbQ-D03MI7R3NCFbMlmOGjm7qKEqpPyqk9p2i8ew7JLQ7yGBJxS2A8UQTPLhwRokrUoagywynxoV1soxqE=> .

 

The IBM Search Engine

 

In an op-ed on Wired, NYU Information Systems chief Vasant Dhar thinks IBM may have a chance at undoing Google's core business. "If IBM did search, Watson would do much better than Google on the tough problems and they could still resort to a simple PageRank-like algorithm as a last resort." Read his reasoning <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzygVh-qRcHMwwcWDbXWTkb-TBE4rrHtcEaZRzZXGQcsEZUDEKX-Af_y8YLTiCndD4ooP3Q8loFzVACuiiXsFazGpRKrCE31foNmOf0LpLoA4aas4y8RhR_M7a-KFKXLnsrwUSsGKxhqHcIzvNtizsuvC0D7pnoD_WcsCf0r17XT3Ug-a2gpoTgPtrq6rxj1QV-7bpt1KWelg1QdroPmpe1Gb> . Dhar admits that IBM would have to swing its positioning into the consumer space - no easy task.

 

Easy Data

 

Data visualization is getting a lot more accessible says internet tech company Silk, which uses a basic content-management system to visualize complex data sets. "Basically what we're teaching people without them realizing it is structur(ed) data is really useful," said Silk co-founder and CEO Salar al-Khafaji. Read more in PandoDaily <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzygOG3ns_M7hpZUdVUW8sAVxNz-SIGaxqQFfcpGvhProjo_od_S631_UY62VnAeDarKBOHLZJA-1UGNxzOoBicHciti9hq0H2xU2zJtFBHfW0mfTqXzFzd3Qt_ZWQRL1GqjglnTFIhHWz2J-8KPBkbJ2i8syd3akljaW1M8h4eBZHmtNIdwtGxOJCaEv2F6flRoe5kI2EfoUDJPtnys25Efp7e0lBA2yusmfkRnkPLuE6Q==> .

 

Digital Pound Sterling

 

The IAB in the UK sees nothing but digital growth in its latest spending report - this one's for the first half of 2013. Among the highlights: "Digital ad spend up 17.5% to record six-month high of over £3 billion or £66 per person online; Mobile now accounts for 14% of total digital spend; 20% of digital display; Consumer goods overtakes entertainment/media as biggest mobile display advertiser." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyhnu-S-7yEtdiaD3FGlchkdemhXk2dzozcJfhNomZmB8g1xlO6tgoZ6yx9WAQShnPSeHEb25NRy8yMgDjXuGJzIGTzzIVihbBU31GvB4ZCzOHi4SYfooelMzz9ZeA5_BWujzSeJZi7-rZ5PjosRxNBZ_via4KDoFX6L3Ju5R9MTPtCQIXkgpEiK2kMeaY4YUf948F0k4M1fWg==>

Xbox Everywhere

 

Microsoft is betting on the success of home entertainment with its Xbox One, due to be released next month. The company is pitching advertisers on the idea of connected devices with the living room TV as the hub. Ad Age <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzygew03JOHT0lNh34DPfNDk3o04g2QDH1gTGecAJckUkcd3q-ehBA4xT6CDrt08F3cztp8phBCfPf1GcEhd4ZvZ_LY52XoNS5fsarwc_WhWY2-8P7XEp36ryiZbkb0piGCoxX8CZgdDLGnVOJeQy2xVP4az_wE6IGbn0X4XTAZAyBUzWjYcsDXIyC2p2pcl2aXLIn--jjM-NedhtpZBA8CXR>  and Adweek <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyh3ZWOUnDJARNluE5bMg5K-F7kgR0HhLLgFmuiMjlx5Trp2L_dzXNWkKSRP0WPeD1KlQjsjWTjIlduYr-zB-VzCQv_VEuz9OI7Luy0l5MrmbsDg45wGwysvTDAAMI_JkZJeclJ1WcJ8GYwM93HdoHuxqTFMmyC2RFfVLEkrL_bE5oErJtYORnp4w0bi8qOHHs_xSL0o4bFSY8bVB0qdNATs77BG5vD2iKg=>  were both at the ANA Masters of Marketing Conference, where Yusuf Mehdi, SVP of online audience business, said, "We are trying to bridge some of the world between online and offline." The idea is that synching up all the devices in a home will bring huge data opportunities to advertisers.

 

The New Deals

 

The growth of the "deals and offers" industry has slowed, and part of the blame could be on the redemption process. At least that's what a group of companies hopes after creating the CardLinx Association <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzygttx9d_u3XRdPDdyX7OJ55DYNfdqJRPQ1JVtliRDW1KhSfZIDe8t3brwJcBZVvyl6YRbclhOrB2J-zaFEXqnD20T4RFCgnOvpGKFHDdO6-NQnBTEsEUlh3CWZYtafKlWQMwE2N3O85oxjGN3zrqPWekW9BmQCObh-KT9q65PiV_LXme2EpeYrVt_u3PJhCkuc=> , which will link offers directly to a credit card, eliminating the need for vouchers and coupons. So far the group is made up of Microsoft, Bank of America, Discover, Deem, Facebook, First Data, Linkable Networks, LivingSocial, Mastercard and others. Microsoft also announced that its Bing Rewards program will be compatible with the CardLinx system. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyiuoK_d0SjuWPyVNnfuznn8EAb4pcdRD2-YH5aWlGMxyzy6ehY1AS4fbB021m2tsz4gLRV_tyhy3IVzPhJ0TS0AOKTZR3hIhz-0SCDkAsfrL4Qh9JdBepdmS7MeXnCjup68geMGlPc7gZZed6PQkKKeau-lZAAew7SpyqLdjQMsiQn1dF_NhuCD6ZvGMRYfs1Q0ON1QsdT23TWCIWq4x4jBzResYS3S6SDd4xefVDxnq0MCSXD9K2aFN_e2inaawOJiK5Ze6sqafQ==> .

 

Google Local Ads

 

Google announced that it's adding some local "spice" to its Product Listing Ads. From the post on the Adwords blog (which seems to have a new product announcement a day): "When someone searches for a product on Google, she may see a Product Listing Ad (PLA) for a local store. When she clicks on the ad, she'll arrive at a local storefront where she can browse a large selection of the store's inventory before she visits in person." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyjBNFE9EU8FJqCsk57A9-4fxtlQpWrkduXZES65CJcRfSSOuPaXidkwmbfdmroiyxdSte8pmNF8ND83y4SjW6VE9yfjJT5zjW1jvJZ6e1LnBZS-lZeZT7_49v7HE7K7T81PjrvxnRXTXDj3W9F95Rvw5eD-DXQA_mIqfErdkzd-WQ==> . PLAs add the long tail as search ads continue to get more graphical. Still more in Internet Retailer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzygo1Bo-gY0vVRO1FaRqmXx_MrowCTyCowixHRaCBYCwh6R3PgVRcac4IHyG8mAeOKEhoKTesJs9Ny4MHTxY1JlSE2Gx0lsmkaFY8O5XS_8ztu_9ypTXbrrBIoGqIP2d0G-H2bgcptt42dbnMINcQ5bDrMjoTpjeF94cXANbx8b8Zffqdg2jbRUZJlXCMoAcuiBnfCf1Pmu2Gw==> .

 

Secret Searches

 

A company made up of ex-Googlers and ex-NSA engineers has released a new product called Disconnect Search, which prevents search engines from tracking users. Right now it's a free product available as a browser add-on, according to TechCrunch. "Even if you never log in to an account, search engines and many websites typically save your searches and connect them to an IP address, which can allow companies to uniquely identify your computer," said Patrick Jackson, CTO of Disconnect. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001-gu_AlHrzyiuoa1UhSAF9Swvw26T_0HT68m8CDz1F7bNAcxxnCVvqBhm19_6jbNlJn2oJ2z2HPeXBuF4O4p9rmrZV0gZhpKHa4wJ5Myqwvb0bl4vq8JZxfzsxVNZnJx9l6DhfTAM7O1RHCfwctSWNiA6rzCBvtkuCEgObovawmMDQDg-OVtvLLJfv5Ht095X54JThRyzrNycuAfckDEQBaaCMrVxG8Mzg3y483pk75-aRQO_jE41u1knektcV05jiha3VKVKyfiisIOAQhG21i1MJVg2IE039rLGn1CWAB200hYN28e13A==> .

DG Loves Rich Media

 

TechCrunch's Anthony Ha reports that DG has made what appears to be an acqui-hire of sorts with its purchase of 11-person rich media vendor Republic Project <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO1sUPuctO0fxHTdQagIE8cxNhNWO5dl9JxTLUBMskFhNA9FTk5mdFwfTEGS9ukzhxdcp09QfnHZEw2XLyPSx7vO9Uaq5EreYpKHOGS_q9h0W7d8n9RpWQHp>  for a reported $1.4 million plus earn-outs. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO0yIEvAaSQhmkYZY_pfPlWaXdWx9UkOoY_jrUxqghLfRgJuDv9I0lz77fKVK82tFA1e__XuSTLU2C8AuRu8RaTw5oLtL1FmJhNZbXk6NoEDQKzZVliggviH8ifmVaU357VK5HhgrzCDV-sD_EqOjrosjdQmFUz9EYXmmReR-KlP5Q==> . Republic pitches a cross-device integration capability with its cloud-based offering. Prior to selling its TV ad distribution business to Extreme Reach this summer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3aeDnYkQlaijbj5I7_jBoRHAp364wFc3wY6jbuoXQToSYDrrQcLcUxff6bQwpOFV5OHYNffK1pSxk-MgpIzT_IBb0Y8-GQnJAys3U8Gk8l2gA4gxgNYiqT9BhhXE7iDpZqmPujfJ5MVEiIY7h7wyiZiJG66QFwyB3oeEhaPo0Wl0In790MkMCUnaFDBKdysGqGuVh2sjQt321AHd-dYS8QV4yXqnGo528=> , DG has a history of purchasing rich media vendors - such as MediaMind <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO0MKfA-olRndRtGPsJnpA0PiFMwfm9XNRL7eH0-7GMe2EufxGfYmjPcQpucKrlQL65w_6XWcfEvYuSoU1wNNBs9KqOB6VOBJTnC5Pa--72PE7G1qykwX4zZeEYgRivVZTsBVGQUznfAitV53AoqH-u8xzDhmF0-Q4djxMBEi6kEwKrnsIXnKauEoy1xYXPcxOCOsIFA8UV4Ew==>  (which was Eyeblaster), Eyewonder <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO2QNXnQCt4T8vJ7o5SteIdlKHhF-1gkop2A18khXghkNsapmCfwebj61YwHqfYgUSsLuSl19fq1wWdoLuBnravKwfJjdoO7lyZ4DdtLT8uJeZQA5zimx3CbXAyQ6VTzvWukcWjgizuEHKcF_ZVSeLLLVfVGPhqqbQmGntkEs9H8MQ==>  and Unicast. It also purchased semantic tech company Peer39 in 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3Fu32n9IjK47Y0ydG8e69lgR8g11ex-pr1UhlL7Cuo7u4NeecDgGiakBiJb5x7CFyfroqKyAQ1ViZm507Wtg22Gr7fFfPSQcHGIFTUAlDQTnJd5El6lNeAleM4I4ecO65sRF2g9KXptzpGp0lJZkOOF96yaIXyOdw=> .

 

Ad Shifting

 

The New York Times reviewed what DVR and on-demand technology is doing to the television industry and found that a lot of networks are experiencing huge jumps in viewer numbers - in some cases seven days after a show premieres. The problem is convincing advertisers to still pay for their time slots knowing that a lot of people fast forward through commercials on recorded TV. Networks like Fox are trying to push viewers to use video on demand rather than DVR because they are able to block fast forwarding that way. "Most viewing is still occurring during the first three days, but if more viewing continues to shift to four-to-seven, or beyond, we won't be getting fully compensated," Joe Earley, COO of Fox Broadcasting, said in an email. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO2rxdEUn8OJg5aK1o_uPUy1DoktC8UUM6usAVqcSSgMWHDvx5QT7wlaYKc7qvlWYFva5QymnvFkoZLdjH0NvdknIp-xk_y6A_KrpOljrIkFU6St4-r3Lg9KYu-bWUnrVFriIowBezD5UCfsXoYa3ir7TRSl8lugjqZa7ruP9ifumeV9aXPe1cil4xRjzQ9lAwuhPVwztz2NO-hBcUdLWX6asKMtVQHAr3o=> .

 

The IBM Search Engine

 

In an op-ed on Wired, NYU Information Systems chief Vasant Dhar thinks IBM may have a chance at undoing Google's core business. "If IBM did search, Watson would do much better than Google on the tough problems and they could still resort to a simple PageRank-like algorithm as a last resort." Read his reasoning <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3NkzmsjVGXE9zxkSMEMf6JWICdZuGGY0WuA8Za_D03VQLEcaRfh78odRrSjVbWlRaB8LBbKkJFqj3qiIurJF8XbyrlQmVGHn-CT8ur0qKXmeLgsWZf0rN1236QS1fHbuYZH8uKqvRG9qsNE1GvHO39BZACk0DoCcVCmvhxujnwv0SzwVHtB2HpWyIvV_f7JE4vTuBoy9AtxJXi5ZVJpBfQ> . Dhar admits that IBM would have to swing its positioning into the consumer space - no easy task.

 

Easy Data

 

Data visualization is getting a lot more accessible says internet tech company Silk, which uses a basic content-management system to visualize complex data sets. "Basically what we're teaching people without them realizing it is structur(ed) data is really useful," said Silk co-founder and CEO Salar al-Khafaji. Read more in PandoDaily <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3yjvZFj5Hdi-AcPLE3t1bvn8uLYJz1F7-uj4eExtSH6R2r6X_iXK3iW4ypRF_hcbO5oGLRmsSoVqxZ5zeMQpJZImUV0b36b2tv37vDlFgWiGShD_jocTj7d7On-MyKMsR9tSq-ky6wNI75632M9KAnyz3gSoZUwJeMXuIs47jYeqCQYX6slHT4wv7mdLU5YSmC3zdycILpfAmXQWU6irMgGebAMjBdDP33y-lmAmxd-w==> .

 

Digital Pound Sterling

 

The IAB in the UK sees nothing but digital growth in its latest spending report - this one's for the first half of 2013. Among the highlights: "Digital ad spend up 17.5% to record six-month high of over £3 billion or £66 per person online; Mobile now accounts for 14% of total digital spend; 20% of digital display; Consumer goods overtakes entertainment/media as biggest mobile display advertiser." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3aRllwJVFM8HXgwxMXNOYH7PuGa81ZQWPgIWJYK6ZWm0qI7STty2nJtfCdoW7aSB8TvmZBq4lpGcdFReZfi1897RBCROw0AyKMmo-vVwZ2jScVczSDlJxtU25ZmnFghLVDPgswPhZ81rhfbJ4jbZamOfVsNo4GT3uSxtvf3IQXVLaZVCpwZiPao3oBbwTla5J3rFrk0_wrjQ==>

Xbox Everywhere

 

Microsoft is betting on the success of home entertainment with its Xbox One, due to be released next month. The company is pitching advertisers on the idea of connected devices with the living room TV as the hub. Ad Age <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO1PlgdC7LtoQiUU5eU0cG6xNKSisRld9mJsZx6zGjNEpy0PMnauUDFt-8KxgHGxFxzKbkV6jwBsDCRpCbKsnXERWOgu5zg-5cq2bPWqdZ4PZC_sg6LXxWWsoH3W9eAak-hf8YDFR07es40mCRy21gjwM0nwDeX-r6azQD4srtMGmPhj9XO_eYR1QKMFgP7Uu2fhrwTMGJswf099KyUW1AI3>  and Adweek <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO0r-gxuOuOJlNRm-cZHnKzMNgGdBLeFm9kxUVC8R3X41v7tGi0xA4-ixe3HLM66ZcxW84k08-o4jajCVJCwX9s3RNcSWqz-Wn2LQKOJWhR95KgggTmn8RuDXLiIDoqpOJboHk6nNvSRoVQHCpKWSemy-NhrbmFfZLX0c-utwW_ApWJPuT-XXjZcJGNXKsw3N3W_kNG4_vBSgCa73F9_TYNhPONrHaKdyz8=>  were both at the ANA Masters of Marketing Conference, where Yusuf Mehdi, SVP of online audience business, said, "We are trying to bridge some of the world between online and offline." The idea is that synching up all the devices in a home will bring huge data opportunities to advertisers.

 

The New Deals

 

The growth of the "deals and offers" industry has slowed, and part of the blame could be on the redemption process. At least that's what a group of companies hopes after creating the CardLinx Association <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO14P1kF0VsfFO4xeIduI1WpfK35P6uBTJqAJ-Bt0hrM5SvRYLpxAOB6NQUYPQ2JyKVtHW9KgQC64lNOjLEg7wSrOy8XGMrAYCj5RX7_ItEpZGkLhbzTsj4W4jm-sICHzuhStuS4K67Ba7MdtZ1xT1J7yhKrZSaDbkTmF5n5E5U_B2GkJ0CqhyI3h5sHcTX5CeA=> , which will link offers directly to a credit card, eliminating the need for vouchers and coupons. So far the group is made up of Microsoft, Bank of America, Discover, Deem, Facebook, First Data, Linkable Networks, LivingSocial, Mastercard and others. Microsoft also announced that its Bing Rewards program will be compatible with the CardLinx system. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO1Sj_iiNwBJdLFh7MPWvEqStSx5OG67IjTUi6vzboMu4GQ1FD4fpQ__O-5QAa1u-THf3I32uJsIh47g97svQHIxZAX69O1vkATz_vQwFuVL82livGggA5llOY1aRDmIIPeWVhmz-AZLbmmwzW1tJesk-QK32HfHnGKHBHJEhCAtQOZcIpbNI3UMQ1VerR2JaIKFMyighZdKtVxfdG-v7q2G4S7Uwna1q9TQNeqTD0G-QoBKIH6-E5aQ_TZDTEn053qdLBYUGyk4Fg==> .

 

Google Local Ads

 

Google announced that it's adding some local "spice" to its Product Listing Ads. From the post on the Adwords blog (which seems to have a new product announcement a day): "When someone searches for a product on Google, she may see a Product Listing Ad (PLA) for a local store. When she clicks on the ad, she'll arrive at a local storefront where she can browse a large selection of the store's inventory before she visits in person." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO0j4LJ8U-t9467ammkY5Ges2HiZFBVMisRHE2KLmw__3mLSetkxUSsesKvUoWi9NyO_u5lQ6jMBJyA3WrOmqlkkCjes0J8OiGxyEmg0q5URLgcKSqsiaNjTGp3jv9JwgUaLz-QGWBhNZLgOXFyoiY9ElySFdPBb62iOhXacgEpO1w==> . PLAs add the long tail as search ads continue to get more graphical. Still more in Internet Retailer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO0-DOG9jaFu3YAsyD2WHZ6g9-wR5Wy-ZZ6kumVnr_0DEEKLUSGp0knGOAnhvV23S-avTGUFvjzldbwMi_cRg1RzSnRpfJiwKdm04zcc2rlslKH33U-PLoXkfKNAcbl29Dymbi7mM61bJbfHCzYnUfnlG_Sr-ZNla5pJhebCdhaKtbJOaU6dh-wJBFJ_mky1oH8IPgAYe4vc5Q==> .

 

Secret Searches

 

A company made up of ex-Googlers and ex-NSA engineers has released a new product called Disconnect Search, which prevents search engines from tracking users. Right now it's a free product available as a browser add-on, according to TechCrunch. "Even if you never log in to an account, search engines and many websites typically save your searches and connect them to an IP address, which can allow companies to uniquely identify your computer," said Patrick Jackson, CTO of Disconnect. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eW_21WhDmO3RKG9BjJLtek7A_H9yWm2gyOFcryRQW0RIXrR8gPv1D7vH6jUsWZakX5KfMelJ9XpPVFWw1pBo8C01uR6Joa6cQMHC3aS4aUch8SssgkqG5v6uaDQ4CZZLVT8kfHW6apIJfCkkMpl-5CZ_iDyKzhg-Ru9dyY2ilOy4Sb6b_vwiKlP7v4xmHDM312AxrGjiCXSVWHncBubmHWQWPGFoAF8BsKoq6UcTQqTJXpa5yTP7DTkEyvDnVnDJNDr2_scElt5Ph6il0gvvnSBPzyYNSO997-Qn8fYWw73hrY4dRPA5KQ==> .

Google Sell-Side 'Active GRP' Coming Soon

 

The Drum reports that that Google's biz dev lead for large publishers, David McMurtrie, told the audience at Thursday's Association of Online Publishers (AOP) event in London that it's time for publishers to start protecting their yields and stop the buy side from taking the lead in the programmatic space: "The power and control is currently with the buyer - they choose the audience and price - they are dictating to you as publishers what the value of your content and inventory is. You need to fight that." Furthermore, McMurtrie spoke to Google's product plans that will impact publishers: "We are currently rolling out viewable impressions and next year will be Active GRPs - our method to track reach across different platforms means tv buyers - used to trading on selling by reach, can look at video in a totally different way, with the accountability and transparency of the Web." Read more from The Drum <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U1UKfoQTr0R0aF1rTiw0TLwUwXJQEvG_28BGGkt9N4OvwTmrMgG1ZZ-h7eaIErZMB-g9hsx1CnyFEKCmPf7bLbqmsJabdyMjBbL5R2DpdihKguJmMdlu-gu3nkBk4NH0DStvvsjYqsaqHXSwJbbGhBhkf49eEiuT91QvGGUO5K9HGlLMEP0RiMP_WZxGrOkTWxS7KfmEuqM0dCdnVnBvrbrWnZ6FONs8SSEoAinaCFh-5rWxqdh_WYp3oHb3RF_NxA=> . As had been previously announced <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U0nN3pwjlv0RkUA1VWO8ieJPUQQ6RmpdY_W7OaC01CBv3sEkfFAIAOZtRqhjsD5uXbj5WHcA8-9hhdKtYFyiWsQ_uRtrEeI6xu1ST_OJs2XWxkiUU-C5eOOjpeQ3vr529qCPQ21mwbP9OLl_MHPAJDjNT1c-R_CZ1jkTwtOuNNpyPpRVTvCcTwPUvuTiDE8FE6SEkC5HTXtpQ==> , Active GRPs are in "limited release" to DFA users (as in advertisers) - and not publishers - according to a Google FAQ <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U3DzB8vThC-XgMHBnZduci4H-L-E_KecVb91jOsQFoG4WJ3VFS-10tnt4zvGnZjWN6HMSKp4nb09_JDQkAex-fUflJ43OrqNaMtV6pSV1i_tXeRZp7jXOUMKbCpJAlo-p8XGsjVlLPRqx97B2M5Wc-s> .

 

Crossing Devices


The New York Times suggests that advertisers know "secrets" about users in an article that looks at cross-device targeting ad technology formerly-known-as "fingerprinting." From the article: "'We're observing your behaviors and connecting your profile to mobile devices,' said Eric Rosenblum, chief operating officer at Drawbridge. But don't call it tracking. 'Tracking is a dirty word,' he said." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U1341a_6hsedc2fnee3T1FaZHJmA0n5CsOTQnGXc8HVvIQfRBgC8fx8u78GY22RTdN9Vec8uDGxUip0rKS4UWH1EwczQH7PIHiKn1jTozLFwcTQ_KocbvgHllzLpDhwDKFGdtXfx3lgxQ5JaFopR0w7NgxiCObHrTpaFBTa5dtSXHGO5eWJeVuIswQjdRkfH90I_uEkvr_P3b9zB2_48-Ek>  And, read this AdExchanger survey <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U2gjerEwpdnJIZWJ2gJARRo1e1pBJQw9zxG2v2iT7BSbn0YxqbZq7gch1w8Ay7Scxlyz5ldNRQk2vUe8Hw9XJvgjUhR7LcgXzmznxYMaQoKcP0v7VQwEHF-4tvRWHZlP2i4hbhqK8XMnxqFYysodAYZvHjy3vSrj5oOsISSOzdntpRJOyVyH0kuZ48182ZujSl18pqgCtwC37MoD2114NIVpuUQX_wOhwA=>  of cross-device companies from March.

 

Scanning Email Lawsuits

 

First Google, now Yahoo. The tech company is being sued in California for scanning emails in order to serve targeted ads, according to Bloomberg. Yahoo didn't comment on the lawsuit, which was filed on behalf of residents of the city of San Bruno as a class-action lawsuit. U.S. District Judge Lucy Koh refused to dismiss a case against Google for email scanning in San Jose last week. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U2Ld03VR3UYL6He06uEPQaihgG7H4WxiOQ7mw6FGpCBJwmCr84MCoZbDDtAguLlmqaRskjDPKxS3OMYlbQ_iLQm0lOTRRTz6MnAquozQMVEj2GwBFpoXi5jM1gpsag_1KObu1BBTVkqFfp-qZH-kml8i3tcBGQtWnHzM4KvxdYllgC7Z5FiVVirUYAfWzyFmyYeP2up4_h5gSfLsmmNITLhmu_j--OmP3Q=> .

 

Twitter Is Better Than Facebook

 

An Econsultancy blog post lists three reasons why Facebook can't beat Twitter when it comes to "social TV" dominance. Among the reasons: the ever-popular hashtag. Twitter is dominated by reaction from users who hashtag properly and the Twitter feed is updated instantaneously. Facebook, not so much. Read the post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U1Rhx1WrPdMMXCuFjYZmWuPj5JnG8bOzOtmenPdAGKIBXALlvJoiIv2rarRe_FPDkiwhW8UebFLrc_BtQ_KgsJrbgy7LLAugihcqtQps_N1j-I6eEXIWmjeWhyHX9C4s2IeB6-Xty00HHtzjNlW5KFYchRS7tSqzBfUXEirTxwQv9KI3aZAUKnrgjokIrrBPo0WOVlCeRa5Zvo8AQ46fYhS> . Facebook Is Better Than Twitter

 

Twitter goes under the pre-IPO microscope, courtesy of The Wall Street Journal, as Twitter's reach comes under question. The article quotes Progressive Corp. CMO Jeff Charney, who prefers Facebook for social media advertising: "'The 200 million-plus Twitter nation is a powerful and influential force that you have to pay attention to.' ... Charney says the insurer will consider spending more as Twitter grows. But Facebook has 'more heft,' he says. 'You just can't ignore Facebook.'" Flash Failures

 

Fab took a leap of faith that flash sales would be a long-term profitable venture, but so far that hasn't panned out as the company laid off 101 people. AllThingsD reached out to Fab and got an email response saying, "We acknowledge that flash sales is a flawed business model." Although the company just secured another round of funding, its total staff loss is now at 37%. CEO Jason Goldberg hasn't personally admitted that flash sales aren't working, but has endeavored to focus on profitability. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U3gGc7Z89RasRKYxAr_y8CRw94KfVkhm_GZwi_Ao7c8kqb7qG-4ozw9KbVvsanamlHieyKCkkuyEEjbUy1w_wSETBtdEWXCY6_D_cxKkdpNqfyfh40jPYlBzHXstAx-qyo3I_O-zVwstZ2i5KNLFCyUyxoUznAwHWg0uFrG5si-DbVJKTjkLpITZt3cKDwR5EKfhFTq_auwxQ==> .

 

Adobe Breach

 

A major security breach at Adobe has left 2.9 million encrypted names and payment information vulnerable, Digital Trends is reporting. Adobe recommends users change their passwords on any sites where the same login information is used and they are in the process of contacting banks about the breach. Furthermore, for those whose credit or debit information was compromised, Adobe is offering a complimentary one-year subscription to a credit-monitoring service. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U1IvqkMtwpyNePA5ZtH-uK8tN_8HPi1H-w-Rf6fyVxfGyLF0HaTEr2VPRs7VAuequ-DOep5Tmx3XSDk3z1rmGT-0C-JZV03DctpyF-3GywueSa4CFJDUKG44PKn8P_1Lmj7YvgPkSO91KHHHwUP7TXn4nohKNGkTCtI3U3QEmZArOXkSc3Ex83z> .

 

Your Own TV

 

IRIS.TV hopes personalization is the key to video engagement, and is bringing that pitch, along with $1.7 million in funding, to the B2B market. The company was founded by the same people who developed Jukebox TV and who come from companies like ABC, Hulu and Disney. Although no specific partnerships are named, the technology will be integrated into a TV and mobile app, says co-founder and CEO Field Garthwaite. Read more on TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U0NzvJYSkqnYOuTYwRnVmEZ2UzCxs8FJPHf4_biyouvgvkVTg6KQLZvng0h73TPWBnpMRqGCVcQ6920IcCTjxmwmrNdnngz0q_M31WDG6Txc6GVqM80Qjb4G6Ehh8QDinsmMNLq1-1R-Q==> . Nick Rau, co-founder of ad effectiveness firm Vizu (which was acquired by Nielsen in 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010RumXjNq6U0RwUZ1mOrRJxIVxPUvx-V72t59_z-03wacqt_Emr2Q3i142zG1EDBsZxdHHXoLXkOWquseExvhkgpWIfEgv40TpncOP8yp-xqDCa63x9giiT7uCdAK4H8czJNDcATaM6W3Uh8kFfVxEYS1AoO5Oko1nauY5f8h45oXRK3U_f0N5g==> ), is evidently an investor.

Instagram Addressing Ads

 

On the (Facebook) Instagram blog yesterday, the mustard seeds of an ads strategy were strewn about as an anonymous Instagram blogger wrote, "In the next couple months, you may begin seeing an occasional ad in your Instagram feed if you're in the United States. Seeing photos and videos from brands you don't follow will be new, so we'll start slow. ... Our aim is to make any advertisements you see feel as natural to Instagram as the photos and videos many of you already enjoy from your favorite brands." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TGLqjVyTodK5dqfVJbQbkCU7yYDCk4q3EJtbQotS2C4SKPp6Sav8O5RHdpKRrOYlqYts1fV01fc_ZJu4fMqSM23wALG60zIzV7MpPQ2EFXLp6j6oLMFVfwksIU7Z4oP4yAn5nP91FdkzOxA4hgCqTdJKUuQq0pFRMNG-QgNu1HisATPpgYwPyUh_Dcuqkpu>  "Natural," dare we say "native," positioning aside...will addressable data drive Instagram media? From here -- undoubtedly. The email address associated with the Instagram login beckons. Facebook's Custom Audience <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019TGLqjVyToe_txd8kbOFbbzYKJfU9ciWaawikOmgVIWa3KK9kzA_3EwX-4Zlel3iVe2LGgJpxOrMrOcz8_tlW50RM5fh9vIbDpBxoXX5t0WRm-Fbp9sNuhzfp5zYeCg050YIU75Y4m17jrsHvPwD8apBJ2t7lfZS5GxSN8ic9vmd_hR0gUsAv1nUgyf_tr1bcNxab4J252c=>  product could extend to, or be segmented for, Instagram audience.

 

Trusty Twitter

 

Twitter's acquisition of MoPub is on the FTC's list of approved transactions, which means its avoiding any antitrust scrutiny. Twitter is gearing up for its IPO, and some estimates have it valued at $10 billion. As Reuters points out, the acquisition of MoPub is going to improve mobile advertising by allowing real-time ads. HyperLocal Conundrum

 

The Sacramento Press has gone the way of Patch and found it hard to monetize a hyperlocal publication. Although it is still up and running, founder Ben Ilfeld told Street Fight it's been a struggle to get advertising dollars and so far no sustainable model has been found. The company is for sale and being run by Ilfeld for the time being. The New Online Video

 

Amid the big success that online video is now experiencing, Meredith and Scripps are turning to original video programming. Scripps is also launching a dedicated online video website, called Ulive, which will archive video clips from some of Scripps' cable shows. "The sites that aggregate video tend to have higher engagement levels," said Jeff Meyer, a Scripps Network Interactive executive and president of Ulive. Compass Labs Drops Facebook

 

Business Insider reports that Facebook Preferred Marketing Developer Compass Labs will no longer work as an intermediary in delivering ads through Facebook's platform. The company's CEO, Dilip Venkatachari, tells BI they'll purse "marketing intelligence" instead. Breaking Down Big Data

 

The newness of "big data" is finally wearing off and leaving people confused or unimpressed, so Jeremy Hlavacek, VP of operations and strategic partnerships at Weather FX, attempts to add some clarity in a piece on MediaPost. He says "big data" is not a whole industry, but rather a market shift. Also, knowing how and when to use data is key to making it work. It should be real-time and recent, rare or unique and advertisers should have realistic expectations, says Hlavacek. The Public Ad Network

 

A source tells TechCrunch's John Constine that former Blue Lithium chief and current RadiumOne CEO Gurbaksh Chahal is readying his company for an IPO. It is rumored that RadiumOne has about $100 million in annual revenue -- if true, this is likely total media spend through the company's ad platform. Constine comments, "It's becoming clearer that TV ad dollars will shift to digital and that businesses can earn money on mobile ads, so RadiumOne seems to think it's ready for the spotlight." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHSrhp0okgUrJQQhw0O7nyX_nLMbAIsNcopG-0flOkQjNG5PrgPXkGqJ5XwKXCCOgchcS5NQDfrca7enuEpFTUVbZJIn4wm8UGudqqPRLZaMEiRTj_Mi72w5vLLdRhuIxuBVrmdOif8kWMK0kc2wXj9q> 

 

Programmatic Demographics

 

Programmatic buying can help advertisers reach Hispanic markets, claims Starcom exec Marla Skiko, who was part of a panel discussion covered by Portada. Skiko mentioned that programmatic is changing the agency discussion around TV. "We want to buy Hispanic audiences in an efficient way. Programmatic trading helps us to do that." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHQisnyHPnqBH7B1wSszCAEfM7Hq55pJSxmL6-VNTfnQYpu4FruTMQgwGLnMtfkv5QtZUMz4LthEsiBWtqv5MTjTUNN2akPl1BXSiAu5DXjhoR3dOmVJErpB003TCDF1uPowikHGix-DwxDiKgMSwVJJ_3IwkGQsXX1TCBjVtE3ZsrAzVOVQ5GoSKWCuHsTQlfZKs_icvTsc-rvJc5xkJ0kNYBf-hBEGp0pa8HHyGl1mcS-J0tG6DVuiqUV5URn26as=> .

 

Foot Data

 

JiWire announced its new Location Conversion Index, which matches a served ad with an in-store visit. The company claims that it is "real" foot traffic because it takes into account things like seasonality and creates a lookalike audience that hasn't been served an ad as a control group. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHTQgW5XbPIJm8g-EMByLZNYoCw2HWHfdSnJOV5eEepKhwwdHK5D0KSYR2k-mN3zVS9fE3jIHQFOMvSdL036-3Tr4Oaqr3245gNI665xh-5IuImyU8qEqVt9iJKaXk5-l1QwAUpNw1v7L7HSVroznxtCtrfMSr6HEaA=> . JiWire told MediaPost that a fashion retailer saw a 32% lift in store visits, measured against an identical audience. Read the story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHQ4DWbyU9LA4Attzlf4qyIHxb8jsNaJJLRKuJKkq3NrSdZ_z5KtaT0G7uGQNhbmosezSsPmSlDopoewP5PShFvMRlHZJsY0Q6PKiy_oF31P_8xdTDSzBSiIkTWDB_35vTpaym9GwoAs2jv5fqijesWv3HXCNpXeMJfED-QnJhHSuJ0hzRckLwekCCpkOUE_KNNbw31B-QnMYr8k4MqO_Npy> .

 

Engineer Shortage

 

Elias Torres, who co-founded landing-page optimizer Performable (which was acquired by HubSpot in 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHTK1O96gmFmp0E3N27jpbF0IDDSACi-GPI5NTpiJwYX8NLbmo4-7XKuA35JvggNPOSFmnjRYBV8SGnQ3Wmfgnl5Bf2_WHCFFpIqOYs0x7Mw9YZ2zdp4_8aAL9iB_eFuPuFhem1yRa2rMexrVr0ygX81P3sfTcQDCMhuawNO5P1GLw==> ), says he spends "80 to 90 percent of his time on recruiting efforts" in his work at HubSpot. Torres tells Boston Business Journal, "Ultimately, HubSpot contacts 400 to 500 engineers a month, and hires two or three of them. In May, the company tripled its talent referral bonus - from $10,000 to $30,000 - as a way to get even more aggressive on recruiting engineers and designers." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHQjKRUUDoNnUiLHGWc9HPa-Q1E7i0dlncuhCZcJO8Jc42PN8XewGEQbwjsOl5Lh-DROrpkfYOLPV9T0aSuXp2LojSWU8AqyzE4E8Y8sS9L0KEGoQbF3LOKYsPRSPSJZ8nFELONYW0omOp7E2ZFIsNlw54HbdaJ9sUQui3SDTzVYGH93B1FITWZQYF0lfpiZlMyW8Q-PfcEQSdprEjqlTdzoc--FYGz-XGc=> .

 

Marketer Buys Tech

 

Staples acquired Runa to improve personalized online shopping, though the terms weren't disclosed. The company will become part of Staples Lab, which has offices in in Seattle and Cambridge already. "With Runa, we're adding technology to better serve our customers with personalized items, offers and delivery estimates, all in real time," said Ronald Sargent, chief executive officer and chairman for Staples. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001f7NWGLiLeHQcjhaRrl2W0TKb0gr8QmxFUEaMlDqNuE9ggNVaeWKdvkARs4fHtT8J8TD-iriyMb1kcBIzifG1GwdFuu9HcGa3gcpIY4_Bi3bp9xBAybTxzKS3gL5AbALBNYjG4iFuzfwwIixzvFSlIkqag-y237DBsKSQp0uLHhK08nGXBhAF-e5_TViD6WEYaOgM5iPImErdehBXu6rTuuJFLbUu-J0CXyvrEfuB1Dk=> .

Tech Raises Venture

 

SAP's venture capital arm is raising money like mad, $1 billion over the last year, in an effort to align itself with enterprise technology. "We're kind of a good pipeline into the things that are to come," said Nino Marakovic, CEO of SAP Ventures. "We want to show customers SAP is forward-thinking." Marakovic told PCWorld that it is expecting a total of 13 exits for its portfolio companies this year. Cross-Device Search

 

Google is putting its cross-device first-party data to use, giving AdWords users a chance to see the effectiveness of search ads at different points in the purchase funnel. The new feature is called "Estimated Cross-Device Conversions" and it relies on Google login data to track users who use Google search, according to The Next Web. "Over time, we'll be adding other conversion types like phone calls and store visits as well as conversions from ads on our search and display network," Sridhar Ramaswamy, SVP for ads and commerce at Google, said on the Inside Adwords <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2dRpbYrKu3B1W57ShSTrow2t8W6WaL5ofVH6vgh9QtELeCK3nkpO7Jrr4wmMvIqnUMXGKhKnGGS6-Omkqn7HBq3jbiOn41TazCZ7IWgUSjpbyLr0vtF54pXwOFB2UtsfClCtNZXAbxEas6ntA2Qde5yOSBmgaFHyuaDdbQx95J30Q==>  blog. And read more on The Next Web <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2fj3WM12h7wOYzM0HWEFWb5x878vdSJ8Wx2szsfWGbWyrMXDhsZKDMY60178F7Fn6aJk7FHKL2buYxcczPTFuFtXFCilwFgrBvlp0cu4F31JG0u_aD_8HqxYNhIIjkz6HTZhyIt1WYnEOkH9lWjm1CHCf1JI6cGB1C6pgzUoC3nQQxPx0RFGiTrIskyCVZnToRSldZlinCFDXMuVl1h-Q5sNh6DlZfLOXl7XbuEmK3OaBX2yU9TYFw6E3If6tFzPdeIizGuWBaDDg==> .

 

MySpace Addressability Grows

 

Specific Media's plans for music site MySpace still aren't clear from an ads and data perspective, but the company is claiming in a release that a rebranding of the site and additional product efforts has led to a 50% increase in website visitors, from 24 million to 36 million unique monthly visitors in a few months. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2eZSyOUa72Qelxp1T-3_D4Hcanvv2lJxh2dt-bJwhz0DacO-MhfvPdsxrjoupqLwTDeQ8E6NiuHH_4901wGGmkbdfoTFeVBSYtJd4MPIkvx_-xqhrVg0Y6xUa7PUTRIhMkeKRuYv41GV1W2OPnyGefz3ukC727uj0bazXYudxLuFBScezmjctsiDyMlvQ_iBMZGjyVv2TuoHQXXdjeVmVZOvHXm_gkshVRiVGL6IVnP7_rVqbEcuyy0YppEF349Cs2lHYLrF3JUAg==> . The release trumpets its valuable 35-or-younger demographic, which the company says is 70% of overall traffic. If MySpace is requiring login tied to email for a good part of these users, scalable addressability of this demo could be interesting to marketers, whether on MySpace or off of it. (Facebook!)

 

The Business Of Social

 

Demandbase launched a B2B social-targeting product today, called Company-Targeted Advertising, which uses Facebook data. The data target not just at the company level, but also allows for targeting of key stakeholders. "Advertisers are missing out on a valuable opportunity to market to businesses across multiple social channels - reaching the millions of executives who are also on social sites while at work on Facebook - at the very moment when they are making important business decisions," said Greg Ott, CMO, Demandbase. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2ciKEwy8Bvzv0N9x4AnxyDVL03uTGp21bufl2_9mgg1bem1r6DvcfMGVm8RA5gUegVtq44xB92KxjRPATtozIFQnhopwGERop__b9I19JMssQBM53keonE91vfmdrXD7PecOKhvxiooRY1cXG0Yi4RRBzLHLEVsHp7hPWEjtcX_s7hJgiicU7fVx-mJBzfEREBLk_XPlfDtPUs4MdPucmWNPlZ-djwy3d5wUa1oP1M_yUYQ1_VoBwba> .

 

Loyalty Costs

 

Fiksu's latest index revealed the cost to acquire a loyal customer is at a record high of $1.90, as of August, up 10 cents from July. Mobile app installs have increased 46% since last year, according to Fiksu's analysis, which is a large part of the reason marketers are pouring so much money into mobile advertising. Companies also are ramping up their spending with Q4, meaning the big holiday rush is right around the corner. "With marketing costs at a record high, and only likely to grow as the holidays approach, now is the time for mobile marketers to hone their campaign strategies -- before the real competition starts," said Micah Adler, Fiksu CEO. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2fgcfd68N5VPKUP2r6JEHil1jBDDpIZ9qv3s80eh24f9WPOV8KRqVkR1jtNHJntZjQTfQDLil3s_64jemxccmTD_bzX_eg91JA9ieeNavgJE_djDhX5J7zh4e2ccH7nFuV1lLh2NRMVejUvS4_8s0MRo1LVxVOx8sIVu2rcQgR2l5oVR8xtCTjGfY1srgBKWnwewOVs2yBIiR5a_uZTcCBFI22FpCdtF7co0tCA9NdmnQ==> , or read the analysis <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2fvINou1Rxdgwsu8aZN3p9jyDxAKoItDmPsOTzZ-6hl39ZQNQ37MkxD1Kl3XfEfugnxjxx5PEniydmgSUuBr3kPxG7hGWfTspe9ie_wcwz1fbAaNMh49qyajoEVkcfMu6UUH_ROgKToTm-0JltY5VrB> .

 

Unfair Programmatic

 

Sales reps could be hindering programmatic progress, The Media Kitchen's Barry Lowenthal writes for Digiday, as those worried about losing commission impede programmatic transactions. One solution that publishers have tried is offering a tiered system, whereby the sales rep gets a smaller commission for programmatic budgets. This still leaves an incentive to stick to direct sales, but as volume increases in programmatic channels it could even out the balance. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2dwBUHbe5WfaarGPATmW70axSR99jWeZdzjExSGhYaLONE53WNxlzc3_MMEUEgRlKVLj8MYnOzeg7jmnXeHrH_VaIGqzqHJHLc95ztJ5rWcxgji0kV8bOkOsC98hur1XlbHK7xPzGHVN17xEbSXIFvc6Z2wSsSZ_cLVq2Jaen1DnLnTzlcM5vqmLwd5l_YoVZk=> .

Calls To Action

 

Convincing people to download your app is one thing; getting them to keep using it is something else. Facebook is giving developers a boost by adding new features to its mobile app ads. Businesses can now choose from various calls to action within its mobile app ads, such as "Book Now," "Watch Video," or "Shop Now." From there, businesses can "send their existing customers directly into customized, specific locations within their apps, such as new content, sales or product promotions," writes Facebook in a blog post. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ztPxkMX6t2c7ivDOpbXhV0RuO68_cSZOOVag1A7tyer-LHEjaRclB3DhBk6kVVkw39WB84KNGr6D2p0mnaf8EP05hIjfnJKomXFDRZ2egfm_mOOEqyF7Hip6jNzQbLtuDOfVRpTA8NPzYcVleAJACX9Wl3uGcJlw3pAZeuirxxKofKpTobVLD6Tf7ERp1qimn91RXckuwRjmfi3njnZINu0ld5UY1gsNgB0qHdUYI6xUPAQBDG3SwY97_Spx9mN8M4Q1vnAx3l_5wmq8zC8Z1A==>

Facebook Sets Sights On TV (Too)

 

Facebook has its eye on TV measurement, the WSJ's Digits blog is reporting, by offering big networks a look at exclusive show data as it looks to match recent initiatives by Twitter. Facebook's data is centered around the usual suspects: interactions, which includes likes, comments and shares a show is generating. "The conversation is being generated by a group that is much more representative of the general population - that means we should have a better signal as it relates to ratings," says Daniel Slotwiner, the head of Facebook's measurement team. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TALKd6k8qNC1pvulpKWXvAU1MsQfu04EFQM9zzI0VPVOQAhSnyQaVX1fjHJVBLauwL0EhZpr1f-eJx2MBvEQwKtzpGNRYLs0IR9LAbx35MzBQ4ySaCP1SDtH_Kvm2B0NOIQdQpRFLXw2gCBO0IStWEWi4w6J2OGSbaW9IdUAxAxd-TIWJnH5tn0q7yXjuptb5hhDeo8SGcuEQ3yoXLoJfQ==> .

 

Native Local

 

Local newspapers are fighting for survival, leading some to adopt native advertising, according to Digiday. In all cases the content is clearly marked as sponsored, but there are still those who feel it's unethical for ads to be presented as stories. The question is how well native advertising can be executed by local papers with limited resources. "It is unclear whether they have the existing resources in both tech and creative production to mobilize here," says Initiative exec Nate Stricker. "It is possible that they'll collaborate with third-party partners to enable it and thus compete -- thereby allowing large brands to achieve national scale in the process." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TALKd6k8qNA-sIKn_uKCARhHeP9vS05uP5dvlUU4vXS_x--9OtjqtujVH4ZAxpVlJdQTK2lPrdoHAHLxR-71XAhFn0OZn3d5qPLfTabJTNgFd8xevqLz1VTLEDMs0WCHODwI21b58sfndverUz07O051mswXlf0DQCHeDatiJEs=> .

 

AudienceStream

 

Tag-management provider Tealium launched its new AudienceStream discovery platform, designed to help marketers segment their audiences across channels and personalize their content. Insights are derived, in part, from a network of vendors across "multiple categories, including email, multichannel messaging, content management, site optimization, customer relationship management, data management, data visualization, business intelligence and data warehousing platforms," says the release. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TALKd6k8qNA7Kl12K11qKRbqgkB4QYEtZaA9JRoSo0Nw4VtXgDhMyFsaL54wjH3K_rU1wJe63VL8PDtrPfMFBRFdpOPq10XuigCpgTvekzGzqj7N00pZj5IlXkS5epJPuCpBsxib5sWNUi3gFzoDT9kS1MzVQrkHtgdDXd6io0Rln_5C7XIIGrbyIvqcxGuxvQQLq54XZX-alsap52nmjQ==> 

 

FTC Stays Focused On Digital

 

The FTC's head of consumer protection, Jessica Rich, gave her first speech in front of marketers since taking her position in June. Adweek covered the event, where Rich made it very clear the FTC would continue its work on keeping advertising honest. "The FTC has long had a focus on national advertising. We're by no means finished," Rich said. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001TALKd6k8qNAn7c-XEW05tu1JZY3xpx-hH_ADupBhLRxh8CgFiyHYN6FxoAxjYwDOvmZiGiWwnNWlqo2e74qcrm_gwY70rlXTkFxxAJJdOInU7hXI3q6SVVzuhQymRK6kpcX77gn1j95utCdJ9yxYLgkZ9WvwdWs1oHYL7P6R2JVis2tLdIwpQOflCvgyiaoiWlkjp3w2gpmFopH7hm7mHLxk4SFaYjovC52r1B2fAi1z4B2icXqNuQ==> .

 

Streaming Audio Segments

 

Data-management platform (DMP) Lotame is adding streaming audio data-segmentation capabilities to Triton Digital's a2x streaming audio ad exchange. According to a release, "The partnership will enable a2x publishers, including Entercom, CBS, Univision and many others, to integrate first- and third-party data from multiple sources in one place." Botnet Burlesque

 

The world of bots and fraudulent traffic take the podium in an article by The Wall Street Journal. The WSJ's Suzanne Vranica talks to media buying firm Accordant Media's co-founder Art Muldoon. Vranica explains, "To sift out bad traffic, Accordant uses a growing cast of security and verification companies, including comScore Inc., DoubleVerify and White Ops. Last year it doubled the money it spent on their services. Accordant also has a swelling blacklist of sites where it won't buy ads. That list has tripled from last year and now includes hundreds of thousands of sites."
